1. what is Hoisting :
	variable and fucntion are moved to top of the scopre during compiltaion.
		
			=> Why it happens :
				=> JS execution 2 phase
					1.Creational  => 1. create execution content	
									 2. Allocate memory
									 3. fucntion and variable declaration
					2.Executional
	
	Eg: console.log(a)  //undefined
		var a = 10;
		
		console.log(b) // referenc error
		let b = 20;
		
2. what is Temporal dead zone :
	=> time between the variable declaration and initialization when access causes error
		applies to:
		let
		const
		
3. Difference between == vs ===
	==  will check for value comparision
	=== will check for value and type of data comparision
	
4. what is closure 
	=> the fucntion that are remember outer scoped varaible to local scoped even after execution
	Eg:	fucntion outer(){
			let count = 10;
			return fucntion inner(){    // used in call backs, data hiding
				count ++
				console.log(count)
			}
		}

11. Difference between async/await vs promise
	async/await used to write promise way of code
	=> cleaner code
	=> easier error handling
	=> readable

≡ÓõÑ Key Differences :

	| Feature        | Promise (.then)        | async/await             |
	| -------------- | ---------------------- | ----------------------- |
	| Syntax         | `.then()` & `.catch()` | `async` + `await`       |
	| Readability    | Can get complex        | Cleaner & easier        |
	| Error Handling | `.catch()`             | `try/catch`             |
	| Code Style     | Chain-based            | Looks synchronous       |
	| Built On       | Native feature         | Built on top of Promise |

		=> prevent multiple API calls.

35. How to reduce bundle size ?
	=> lazy load
	=> tree shake : Tree shaking removes unused imports, functions, services, and modules from the production build.

			Eg : ΓÙÔ Bad (may include unused service)
					@NgModule({
					  providers: [MyService]
					})
					export class AppModule {}

				Γ£à Best practice (tree-shakeable)
					@Injectable({
					  providedIn: 'root'
					})
					export class MyService {}
					Γ£õ If MyService is never used ΓÁÈ removed automatically

		=> It works by default in production builds.  => ng build --configuration production

	=> remove unused library
	=> standalone component
	=> compression

46. How to Prevent XSS (Interview Answer)
	Γ£õ Escape user input
	Γ£õ Avoid innerHTML
	Γ£õ Use Angular built-in sanitization
	Γ£õ Use Content Security Policy (CSP)
	Γ£õ Validate input

	=> XSS (Cross-Site Scripting) is a client-side attack where malicious scripts are injected into web pages and executed in the user's browser. It can be prevented using input sanitization and AngularΓÇÕs built-in template escaping.

	=> CSRF is an attack where a logged-in user's browser is tricked into sending unauthorized requests to a trusted server. It is prevented using CSRF tokens, SameSite cookies, or by using token-based authentication like JWT instead of cookies.
	
	
47. what is an Angular library ?
	=> For sharing the UI compoents, services, , directives, and utilities access multiple projects
	=> An Angular library is a reusable package that contains:
		=> Component
		=> Services
		=> Pipes
		=> Directives
		=> Utilities
		
		that can import into multiple projects
		
		
	=> Example use cases:
		Common Button Component
		Shared Auth Service
		Common Header/Footer
		Custom Validators
		
	steps :
			steps 1:
				=> ng generate library shared-ui
				
				=> projects/
					 ΓõõΓõÇΓõÇ shared-ui/
						 ΓõõΓõÇΓõÇ src/
							 ΓõõΓõÇΓõÇ lib/
								 Γõ£ΓõÇΓõÇ shared-ui.module.ts
								 Γõ£ΓõÇΓõÇ shared-ui.component.ts
									
			step 2 : generate component inside the library
				=> ng g component button --project=shared-ui

			step 3: Export Component From Library Module
			
			step 4 : ng build shared-ui  => dist/shared-ui/ -> this deployable
			
			step 5 : Version Your Library  
				=> in the - projects/shared-ui/package.json -> "version" : "1.0.0"
				
			step 6 : Publish Internally (3 Enterprise Options)
			
					Option 1:  Private NPM Registry (Recommended) -> 1. Nexus
								=> publish => npm publish
								=> install in any project => npm install @company/shared-ui
						
					Option 2:  Git Based Installation (Quick Setup)
								=> npm install git+https://github.com/company/shared-ui-lib.git
								
					Option 3 : Local Tar Package (Offline Mode)
								=> npm pack -> It will create .tqz file 
								=> npm install shared-ui-1.0.0.tgz

						
															 
															
			
			Step 6: Use Library in Your Application
				
				import { SharedUiModule } from 'shared-ui';

					@NgModule({
					  imports: [
						SharedUiModule
					  ]
					})
					export class AppModule { }
					
			step 6 : Use Library Component in Any Component HTML
				=> <lib-button></lib-button>

	| Feature         | JavaScript        | TypeScript               |
	| --------------- | ---------------   | ------------------------ |
	| Typing          | Dynamic           | Static                   |
	| Compile Step    | ΓÙÔ No             | Γ£à Yes                   |
	| Error Checking  | Runtime           | Compile time             |
	| OOP Support     | Limited           | Strong (Interface, Enum) |
	| Tool Support    | Basic             | Excellent (IntelliSense) |
	| Scalability     | Hard              | Easy                     |
	| Angular Support | ΓÙÔ Not supported  | Γ£à Required              |


49. What are the ES6 features :
	=> ES6 (ECMAScript 2015) introduced many modern JavaScript features that make code cleaner, shorter, and easier to maintain.

	1. Let and Const :
		Purpose
		=> Block-scoped variables (safer than var).
			Example
				let count = 10;
				count = 20;   // allowed

				const PI = 3.14;
				// PI = 3.15; ΓÙÔ not allowed

		=>	Real-time Use Case
				In a React or Angular component, constants like API URLs should not change.
				const API_URL = "https://api.company.com/users";

	2. Arrow Functions
			Purpose
				=> Shorter function syntax and automatic this binding.
				Example
					const add = (a, b) => a + b;
					console.log(add(5, 3)); // 8

			=> Real-time Use Case :
				Used heavily in React event handlers or array operations.
	

	3. Template Literals
			Purpose
				String interpolation using backticks.
			Example
			let name = "Roy";
			let message = `Hello ${name}`;
			console.log(message);

			=> Real-time Use Case :
			 	Generating dynamic UI messages or API URLs
					let userId = 10;
					let url = `https://api.company.com/users/${userId}`;

	4. Destructuring
			Purpose
				Extract values from objects/arrays easily.
			Example
			const user = {
			  name: "Roy",
			  age: 30
			};
			const {name, age} = user;
			console.log(name);

		=>	Real-time Use Case :
				Very common in React props or API responses
	5. Spread Operator (...)
			Purpose
				Copy or merge arrays/objects.
			Example
				const arr1 = [1,2];
				const arr2 = [...arr1, 3,4];
				console.log(arr2);

	6. Default Parameters
			Purpose
				Provide default values to function parameters.
			Example
			function greet(name = "Guest"){
			   console.log(`Hello ${name}`);
			}
			greet(); // Hello Guest

		=>	Real-time Use Case
				Handling optional parameters in API functions

	7. Classes
			Purpose
				Object-oriented syntax in JavaScript.
			Example
				class Person {
				   constructor(name){
				      this.name = name;
				   }
				   greet(){
				      console.log(`Hello ${this.name}`);
				   }
				}
				const p = new Person("Roy");
				p.greet();

			=>	Real-time Use Case :
					Creating models or services in large applications

	8. Modules (Import / Export)
		Purpose
			Split code into reusable files.

50. Example for NgRx and where we used in our project ?
		=> Claim List Page :
			-> Fetch claims from API
			-> Show claims in table
			-> Update claim status
			-> Show loading indicator
			-> Cache claims so multiple components can use them

	=> With NgRx:
		  Single centralized state store
				Component ΓÁÈ Action ΓÁÈ Reducer ΓÁÈ Store ΓÁÈ Component
			                     ΓÁô
			                  Effect ΓÁÈ API

		Main NgRx Components :
			Store
			Actions
			Reducer
			Effects
			Selectors

	1. Action (Trigger Event)
			Action represents something that happened in the application.
		=> Real-time Meaning :
				User opens Claim List Page ΓÁÈ dispatch loadClaims.

	2. Reducer (Update State)
			Reducer updates the store state.
		=> Real-time Meaning
			Reducer updates:
				loading = true
				claims = API response

	3. Effect (API Calls)
			Effects handle side effects like API calls.
		=> Real-time Meaning :
			Action ΓÁÈ Effect ΓÁÈ API call ΓÁÈ Dispatch Success Action

	4. Selector (Read Store Data)
			Selectors help components read data from store.

	5. store 

	Flow Diagram :
		Component
		   |
		dispatch Action
		   |
		Actions
		   |
		Effects ΓÁÈ API Call
		   |
		Success Action
		   |
		Reducer
		   |
		Store Updated
		   |
		Selector
		   |
		Component UI Updated

	Where did you use NgRx? 
		=> In our Angular insurance project we used NgRx for centralized state management. For example, in the Claim module we used actions to trigger 
		   claim loading, effects to call backend APIs, reducers to update the store, and selectors to retrieve claim data in components. 
		   This helped avoid multiple API calls and maintain a single source of truth


	1. Where is Memory Allocated ?
		->  The store is allocated in the browser's JavaScript heap memory.
		-> So the store lives as long as the Angular app is running in the browser tab.

	2. Where Do Components Access the Store ?
		-> Components inject it.
				constructor(private store: Store) {}

	3. How Can the Entire Store Be Cleared ?
		Yes, there are multiple ways to reset the store.
		1. Method 1 (Most Common) ΓÇõ Logout Action -> logout action and reset state.
		2. Method 2 ΓÇõ Meta Reducer (Best Practice) -> if (action.type === '[Auth] Logout') {
													      state = undefined;
													    }
		3. Method 3 ΓÇõ Browser Refresh
			Since store is in memory, refreshing browser clears it.
				Page Refresh
				   ΓÁô
				Angular reloads
				   ΓÁô
				Store recreated

51. NgRx Store vs BehaviorSubject (Angular State Management) ?
		| Feature      | NgRx Store              | BehaviorSubject Service    |
		| ------------ | ----------------------- | -------------------------- |
		| State type   | Global state management | Local/shared service state |
		| Architecture | Redux pattern           | Simple RxJS                |
		| Complexity   | High                    | Low                        |
		| Boilerplate  | More files              | Minimal code               |
		| Best for     | Large applications      | Small/medium features      |

	=> BehaviorSubject is a simple RxJS-based state sharing mechanism typically used inside Angular services for small or localized state management. 
	   NgRx Store, on the other hand, follows the Redux pattern and provides a centralized global store with actions, reducers, effects, and selectors. 
       NgRx is better suited for large enterprise applications where predictable state management, debugging, and scalability are important.


52. what are angular injection where and how it is used in terms of insrurance project ?
	=> In Angular, Injection usually refers to Dependency Injection (DI).
	=> It is a design pattern where Angular automatically provides required objects (services, classes) to components instead of you creating them manually.

	2. Why Angular Uses Dependency Injection
		Benefits:
			Loose coupling
			Reusable services
			Easy testing
			Centralized logic
		Instead of:
			const service = new ClaimService();
		Angular does:
			constructor(private claimService: ClaimService) {}
		=> Angular creates the instance automatically.

	Types of Angular Injectors
		Angular has hierarchical injectors :

			Injector Level			Example
			Root Injector			providedIn: 'root'
			Module Injector			Provided in module
			Component Injector		Provided in component

	Eg : @Injectable({
		  providedIn: 'root'
		})
	=> 	Means: One instance for entire application

53. what are injection token ?
		=> InjectionToken is a unique identifier used in Angular dependency injection to provide and inject values that are not classes, 
		   such as configuration objects or interfaces.

	Step 1 ΓÇõ Create Injection Token :
		import { InjectionToken } from '@angular/core';
		export const API_URL = new InjectionToken<string>('API_URL');

	Step 2 ΓÇõ Provide Value in Module :
		@NgModule({
		  providers: [
		    { provide: API_URL, useValue: 'https://insurance-api.com' }
		  ]
		})
		export class AppModule {}

	Step 3 ΓÇõ Inject in Service
		import { Inject } from '@angular/core';
		@Injectable({
		providedIn: 'root'
		})
		export class ClaimService {
			constructor(
			private http: HttpClient,
			@Inject(API_URL) private apiUrl: string
			) {}
				getClaims() {
				return this.http.get(`${this.apiUrl}/claims`);
			}
		}


54. What is TestBed in Angular ?
	=> In Angular unit testing, TestBed is the main testing utility provided by Angular to configure and create an Angular testing environment

	=> It allows you to:
			Configure testing module
			Create component instances
			Inject services
			Compile templates
			Mock dependencies
		=>	It works very similar to AngularΓÇÕs @NgModule, but only for test cases.

		Eg: beforeEach(() => {
			  TestBed.configureTestingModule({
			    declarations: [UserComponent],
			    providers: [UserService],
			    imports: []
			  });
			});

	1. How do you mock a service ?
		=> Mocking a service in Angular means replacing the real service with a fake implementation during testing so that:
				You avoid real API calls
				You control the data returned
				Tests become faster and predictable

	2. How do you test HTTP calls ?
		=> Testing HTTP calls in Angular is usually done using HttpClientTestingModule and HttpTestingController.
		   This allows you to mock backend API calls and verify requests without hitting the real server.

	3. How do you test Observables in Angular ?
		=> Observables are tested by subscribing to them and asserting the emitted values. 
		   For asynchronous observables we use JasmineΓÇÕs done() or Angular utilities like fakeAsync and tick(). 
		   For HTTP observables we use HttpClientTestingModule and HttpTestingController to mock responses.

	4. How do you test NgRx store in Angular ?
		=> NgRx store can be tested by testing reducers, selectors, actions, and effects separately. 
		   For component testing we use provideMockStore to create a mock store and verify dispatched actions and selected state. 
		   Effects are tested using provideMockActions, and reducers are tested as pure functions.

	5. How do you test async operations in Angular ?
		=> Testing async operations in Angular means verifying code that runs asynchronously, such as:
				HTTP calls
				Promises
				setTimeout / setInterval
				Observables
				NgRx effects
				
			Angular provides special utilities for this.
				The most common ones are:
					done()
					async / waitForAsync
					fakeAsync
					tick()
					flush()

			=> Angular provides utilities like done(), waitForAsync, and fakeAsync to test asynchronous code. 
			   The most commonly used approach is fakeAsync with tick() which allows us to simulate asynchronous behavior 	
			   such as promises, timers, and observables in a synchronous testing environment

	6. How do you test @Input, @Output, and Reactive Forms in Angular ?
			@Input ΓÁÈ Assign value to component property and run detectChanges()
			@Output ΓÁÈ Use spyOn() on EventEmitter.emit
			Reactive Forms ΓÁÈ Test form initialization, validation, and submission logic using FormGroup controls.

		| Type       | Purpose               | Example              |
		| ---------- | --------------------- | -------------------- |
		| Structural | Change DOM structure  | `*ngIf`, `*ngFor`    |
		| Attribute  | Change style/behavior | `ngClass`, `ngStyle` |
		| Component  | UI with template      | `@Component`         |

56. Angular Decorators Table :
		| Type          | Decorator       | Used On           | Purpose                              | Example                                   |
		| ------------- | --------------- | ----------------- | ------------------------------------ | ----------------------------------------- |
		| **Class**     | `@Component`    | Class             | Defines a UI component with template | `@Component({selector:'app'})`            |
		| **Class**     | `@Injectable`   | Class             | Marks class for dependency injection | `@Injectable({providedIn:'root'})`        |
		| **Class**     | `@Directive`    | Class             | Creates custom directive             | `@Directive({selector:'[appHighlight]'})` |
		| **Class**     | `@Pipe`         | Class             | Creates custom pipe                  | `@Pipe({name:'uppercase'})`               |
		| **Property**  | `@Input`        | Property          | Parent ΓÁÈ Child data binding          | `@Input() name: string;`                  |
		| **Property**  | `@Output`       | Property          | Child ΓÁÈ Parent communication         | `@Output() event = new EventEmitter();`   |
		| **Property**  | `@ViewChild`    | Property          | Access child component/view          | `@ViewChild('ref') el;`                   |
		| **Method**    | `@HostListener` | Method            | Listen to DOM events                 | `@HostListener('click')`                  |
		| **Method**    | `@HostBinding`  | Property/Method   | Bind value to host element           | `@HostBinding('style.color')`             |
		| **Parameter** | `@Inject`       | Constructor param | Inject dependency manually           | `constructor(@Inject('API') api)`         |
		| **Parameter** | `@Optional`     | Constructor param | Dependency optional                  | `@Optional() service`                     |

9. diff between String, string buffer, string builder

	Feature				String 			String buffer 				String builder
	mutable 			No				yes							yes
	thread safe 		yes 			Yes							No
	performce			slow  			medium						faster

≡Óõ╣ Why StringBuffer is Thread-Safe?

	=> StringBuffer methods are synchronized.
		
		Example (inside JDK)
		public synchronized StringBuffer append(String str) {
		    toStringCache = null;
		    super.append(str);
		    return this;
		}
		
		≡ÓõÀ Key point:
				synchronized ensures only one thread can modify the object at a time
				Prevents race conditions
				Guarantees data consistency
		So, when multiple threads try to modify the same StringBuffer, access is serialized.

≡Óõ╣ Why StringBuilder is NOT Thread-Safe?

		=> StringBuilder methods are NOT synchronized.
		
		Example
		public StringBuilder append(String str) {
		    super.append(str);
		    return this;
		}
		
		≡ÓõÀ Key point:
				Multiple threads can modify it at the same time
				Leads to data corruption
				Faster because no locking overhead

44. what is live lock ?
	=> live lock is situation where threads are active and running, but no actual progress is made beacsue they keep resposnidng each 				other.
		=> Threads are not blocked
		=> threads are not waiting
		=> CPU is being used
		=> but no work is getting completed
		
	=> How to prevent :
		=> add random time for retrying
		=> limit retry attempt
		=> better lock strategy
		=> avoid busy waiting.  wait(), notify()
		
45. What is Parrallel streams :
	=> allow stream operation to run parallel using multiple threads to improve performce for large appln
	Eg: list.parallelStream().forEach(n-> sout(n))  => Note : order is not guaranteed.
		
		=> improve CPU usage					=> use forEachOrdered() if order needed
		=> multiple threads
		=> faster heavy loads.
		

45. Diff between :

	DeadLock 							Live Lock
	thread are blocked					thread are running
	waiting forever						actively retrying
	No CPU usage						High CPU usage
	Resource locked						No Resource lock
	
	
46. Both Comparable and Comparator are used for object sorting in Java.
	=> Comparable Inteface:
	
		=> used to define natural ordering sort
		=> has only one method -> compareTo(Object o)
		
			Eg: class Employee implemets Comarable<Employee>{
			
				priavte Integer id;
				private Sring name;
				
				Employee(Integer id, String name){
					this.id = id;
					this.name = name;
				}
				
				public int compareTo(Employee e){
					return this.id = e.id;
				}
				}
				
	=> Comparator Interface
		=> Used to define external sorting logic
		=> create mutliple sorting logics
		=> have one method -> compare(Object o1, Object o2);
		
		Eg: public class NameComparator implemets Comparator<Employee>{
		
			public int compare(Employee e1, Employee e2){
				return e1.name.compareTo(e2.name);
			}
		}
		
		
47. FlatMap : examples
	Eg 1: 
		List<List<String>> list = Arrays.asList(
                Arrays.asList("java", "python"),
                Arrays.asList("Angular", "react"),
                Arrays.asList("js", "php")
        );

        list.stream().flatMap(l-> l.stream()).forEach(n-> System.out.println(n));
		
	Eg 2 :
	 List<List<Integer>> numbers = Arrays.asList(
                Arrays.asList(1, 2, 3),
                Arrays.asList(3, 4, 5),
                Arrays.asList(5, 6, 7)
        );

        List<Integer> num = numbers.stream().flatMap(l-> l.stream()).distinct().collect(Collectors.toList());

        System.out.println(num);

    String s2 = "ACD";

    String s3 = s1.concat(s2);

        Set<String> s4 = new HashSet<>();


        System.out.println(Arrays.stream(s3.split(""))
                .collect(Collectors.groupingBy(Function.identity(),Collectors.counting()))
                .entrySet()
                .stream().filter(ele-> ele.getValue() > 1)
                .map(e-> e.getKey())
                .collect(Collectors.joining()));  // AC
				
				
53. Find indices whose sum equals target.

	Example
	[2,7,11,15], target=9
		
		int arr[] = {2,17,11,7}; // target=9
        for (int i = 0; i < arr.length; i++) {
            for (int j = i+1; j < arr.length; j++) {
                if(arr[i] + arr[j] == 9){
                    System.out.println(arr[i]  + " " + arr[j]);
                }
            }
        }

		Eg:  String str = "banana";
			 Arrays.stream(str.split(""))
                .collect(Collectors.groupingBy(Function. identity(), Collectors.counting()))
                .entrySet().stream()
                .sorted(Map.Entry.comparingByValue())
                .forEach(n-> System.out.println(n));

57. What is Lookups
	=> Lookup means quickly finding a value or record using a key or reference.
	
		eg 1: Programming Example (Java Map Lookup)
				Map<Integer, String> map = new HashMap<>();
				map.put(101, "Manju");
				map.put(102, "Rahul");

				// Lookup
				System.out.println(map.get(101));
				
		eg 2: Database Lookup Example (SQL)
			SELECT name 
			FROM employee 
			WHERE emp_id = 101;
			
			≡ÓÀÊ emp_id = 101 is the lookup key
			
			
58. How Springboot App works and do thing internally automatically
	
		Simulating in plain java as below :
		
		≡ÓÜÇ SpringBootSimulator.java
			
			import java.util.*;

			class HelloController {

				public String hello() {
					return "Hello World from Spring Boot Simulation";
				}
			}

		public class SpringBootSimulator {

			public static void main(String[] args) {

				System.out.println("Starting Application...");

				// Step 1: Create IOC Container
				Map<String, Object> container = new HashMap<>();

				// Step 2: Create Bean
				HelloController controller = new HelloController();
				container.put("helloController", controller);

				// Step 3: URL Mapping
				Map<String, String> urlMapping = new HashMap<>();
				urlMapping.put("/hello", "helloController");

				// Step 4: Simulate Request
				String requestUrl = "/hello";

				HelloController bean =
						(HelloController) container.get(urlMapping.get(requestUrl));

				String response = bean.hello();

				System.out.println("Response: " + response);
		}
	}

	
		=> Γ¡É Architecture Diagram Explanation (Tell Verbally)
			
				Main Class
					ΓÁô
				ApplicationContext Created
					ΓÁô
				Component Scan
					ΓÁô
				Bean Creation
					ΓÁô
				Dependency Injection
					ΓÁô
				Embedded Server Startup
					ΓÁô
				DispatcherServlet Mapping
					ΓÁô
				Controller Execution


59. If multiple interfaces have the same default method and a class implements both, Java will NOT automatically choose one. 
	
	=> It causes compile-time error.
	
	=> Choose One Interface Explicitly
		
		class Test implements A, B {
			@Override
			public void show() {
				A.super.show();   // Calls A's method
			}
		}
		
60. Pre-Processor and Post-Processor diff
	=> Pre-Processor : 
		1. ≡ÓÀÊ A Pre-Processor is something that executes BEFORE the main logic/action/request is processed.
			Examples:
				Authentication check
				Request validation
				Logging request data
				Adding headers
				
	==> Post-Processor : ≡ÓÀÊ A Post-Processor runs AFTER the main logic/action/request is completed.
			Used for:
				Logging response
				Modifying response
				Cleanup tasks
				Auditing

	==>  CompletableFuture is java classs used to perform asyncrnous, non blobking, opeartion and handle result when they become avaibale
	
	=>  Γ£õ Non-blocking
		Γ£õ Callback based
		Γ£õ Better performance
		
	=> Γ£à Important Methods (Interview Must-Know)
		1. runAsync() ΓÁÈ No Return Value
		2. supplyAsync() ΓÁÈ Returns Value
		3. thenApply() ΓÁÈ Transform Result
		4. thenAccept() ΓÁÈ Consume Result
		5. thenRun() ΓÁÈ No Input No Output

64. OOPS:
	==> Encapsulation ΓÇô Data Hiding & Protection
		-> Encapsulation means wrapping data (variables) and methods into a single unit (class) 
			and restricting direct access to the data
			
			Eg: Bank Account
					You cannot directly access balance
					You must use deposit() / withdraw()
					
			Γ£à Benefits
				Improves security
				Controls how data is modified
				Easier maintenance
				
	==> Inheritance ΓÇô Code Reusability
		-> Inheritance allows a child class to acquire properties and behavior of a parent class.
			
			Eg: Bank Account
					you have Gold accont class have some intrest calculate method
					same can used in Slilver account class
			
	==> Polymorphism ΓÇô One Thing, Many Forms
		-> Same method name but different behavior depending on the object.
				
				Types :
					Compile-time (Method Overloading)
  					Run-time (Method Overriding)
					
			Eg : Payment Method
					pay() ΓÁÈ Card
					pay() ΓÁÈ UPI
					pay() ΓÁÈ Cash
	
	==> Abstraction ΓÇô Hide Implementation Details
		-> Showing only essential features and hiding internal logic.
			
			payment and sendSMS these will just give us methods, 
			not expose the implementation
			
65. ≡Óõ╣ Why static methods cannot be overridden?
			Overriding depends on runtime polymorphism, and:
			Static methods belong to the class
			They are resolved at compile time, not runtime
			So dynamic method dispatch does NOT apply to static methods.
			
		≡Óõ╣ What actually happens? ΓÁÈ Method Hiding
			If a child class defines a static method with the same signature as a static method in the parent class, it is called method hiding, not overriding.
			
66. ≡Óõ╣ How ExecutorService Works in Java (Step-by-Step)
	
	==> ExecutorService is part of the java.util.concurrent package and is used to manage and execute multiple threads efficiently 
		without creating threads manually.
			
		1∩╕Â. Problem Without ExecutorService
			ΓÙÔ Problems:
				Too many threads ΓÁÈ OutOfMemoryError
				No control over thread lifecycle
				Poor performance due to frequent thread creation
			
		2∩╕Â. What ExecutorService Does
				ExecutorService:
					Creates a thread pool
					Accepts tasks (Runnable / Callable)
					Assigns tasks to available threads
					Manages queueing, reuse, and shutdown
		
		
67. JOINS in SQL

	=> 1∩╕Â. INNER JOIN ΓÇô Matching Records Only
		=> Returns rows only when there is a match in both tables.
		
	=> 2∩╕Â. LEFT JOIN (LEFT OUTER JOIN)
		=> Returns all rows from left table + matching rows from right table.
	
	=> 3. RIGHT JOIN (RIGHT OUTER JOIN)
		=> Returns all rows from right table + matching rows from left table.
		
	=> 4. FULL JOIN (FULL OUTER JOIN)
		=> Returns all records from both tables
		   Non-matching rows contain NULL
		   
	=> 5. CROSS JOIN ΓÇô Cartesian Product
		=> Returns all possible combinations.
	
	=> 6. SELF JOIN in SQL (with Real-Time Examples)
	
		=> A SELF JOIN is when a table is joined with itself.
			-> when table having emp_id,  name, manager_id
			
			Eg : SELECT 
					e.name AS employee,
					m.name AS manager
				FROM Employee e
				LEFT JOIN Employee m
				ON e.manager_id = m.emp_id;

		
	≡ÓÃ» Real-Time Interview Use Cases
		INNER JOIN ΓÁÈ Active users with orders
		LEFT JOIN ΓÁÈ Customers without orders
		RIGHT JOIN ΓÁÈ Products not sold
		SELF JOIN ΓÁÈ Employee-Manager hierarchy
		FULL JOIN ΓÁÈ Data reconciliation
		
68. How do you handle configuration changes without redeploying all services?

	=> Centralized Configuration Server (Most Common)
	
		How it works
			Store configs in Git / Vault / S3
			All services read config from a central config server
			Config changes do not require redeployment
		
	=> Dynamic Refresh (@RefreshScope)
	
		Allows beans to reload configuration at runtime.
			@RefreshScope
			@Component
			public class PaymentConfig {
				@Value("${payment.timeout}")
				private int timeout;
			}
			
	=> Environment Variables (Container-Friendly)
			Very common in Docker & Kubernetes.
	
	=> Feature Flags / Toggles (Business Config)
	
		if(featureFlagService.isEnabled("NEW_PAYMENT_FLOW")) {
			newFlow();
			} else {
				oldFlow();
		}
		
	=> Database-Stored Configuration

71. How many String Objects will be created for String s1 = new String("ankit");
	=> Γ£à Answer: 2 String objects are created
	
		-> "ankit" ->  This literal is checked in the String Constant Pool.
					   If "ankit" is not already present, one object is created in the SCP.
				
		-> new String("ankit") -> The new keyword always creates a new object in the heap.

74. | Feature     | HashMap    	| LinkedHashMap        | TreeMap        |
	| ----------- | ----------  | -----------------    | -------------- |
	| Ordering    | ΓÙÔ No       | Γ£à Insertion order   | Γ£à Sorted order |
	| Internal DS | Hash Table  | Hash Table + DLL     | Red-Black Tree |
	| Performance | Γ¡É Fastest  | Γ¡ÉΓ¡É Medium         | Γ¡É Slowest      |
	| Null Key    | Γ£à One      | Γ£à One              | ΓÙÔ Not allowed  |
	| Null Values | Γ£à Allowed  | Γ£à Allowed          | Γ£à Allowed      |
	| Thread-safe | ΓÙÔ No       | ΓÙÔ No               | ΓÙÔ No           |
	
	=> HashMap fails when order or thread safety is required, 
	=> LinkedHashMap fails in memory-critical systems, 
	=> TreeMap fails with null keys, bad comparators, or when high performance is needed.
	
	
	
75. Behaviour of HashMap in Multi-threaded env.

	=> ≡ÓÀÊ HashMap is NOT thread-safe.
			Using it concurrently without synchronization can lead to data corruption, 
			lost updates, exceptions, and (in older Java) infinite loops.
			
	≡Óõ┤ What goes wrong with HashMap in multi-threading?

		1. Data Inconsistency (Lost Updates)
		2. Internal Structure Corruption (Very Dangerous)
		3. ConcurrentModificationException (Fail-Fast)
		4. Visibility Issues
		5. NullPointerException (Rare but Real) => During concurrent resize, a thread may read a partially updated bucket.
		

76. ≡Óõ╣ What is Method Hiding in Java?

	=> Method hiding happens when a subclass declares a static method with the same name and parameters 
		as a static method in the parent class.
		
		class Parent {
			static void show() {
				System.out.println("Parent show()");
			}
		}

		class Child extends Parent {
			static void show() {
				System.out.println("Child show()");
			}
		}

	=> ≡Óõì What @Lazy Changes  :
				Bean is NOT created at startup
				Bean is created only when first requested
				Improves startup performance


78. why lambda inroduced ?

	=> Lambdas were introduced to reduce boilerplate code, enable functional programming, 
		support the Streams API, and make Java code more readable, expressive, and 
		scalableΓÇõespecially for collections and concurrency.
		
	Advanctages :
	1. Enable Functional Programming in Java
	2. Better Support for Streams API
	3. Cleaner Concurrency Code
	4. Encourage Declarative Programming  : employees.stream()
											 .filter(e -> e.getAge() > 30)
											 .toList();
	5. Reuse via Functional Interfaces
	6. Improve Readability & Maintainability.
	
	
79. Peek() method in streams
	=> the peek() in java stream method is mainly used for debugging, logging or monitering elements 
	   while a stream pipeline is executing, without modifying the streams
	
	Eg : Stream<T> peek(Consumer<? super T> action)
	
			1. It performs the given action on each element
			2. Returns the same stream
			3. It is an intermediate operation
			4. Executes only when a terminal operation is called
			
		Eg:	employees.stream()
			.peek(e -> System.out.println("Original: " + e))
			.filter(e -> e.getSalary() > 50000)
			.peek(e -> System.out.println("After filter: " + e))
			.map(Employee::getName)
			.peek(name -> System.out.println("Mapped name: " + name))
			.toList();
			
80. Can Optional be null?
	=> An Optional reference can be null, but it should never be null in practice. 
		If it is, the design is wrong and defeats the purpose of using Optional
		

81. How to Make a Class Serializable ? just make implements your class to Serializable (Marker interface)
	=> import java.io.Serializable;

		class Employee implements Serializable {
			int id;
			String name;
			double salary;
		}
		
	Eg : ≡Óõ╣ Serialize (Object ΓÁÈ File)
	
			ObjectOutputStream oos =
				new ObjectOutputStream(new FileOutputStream("emp.ser"));
			oos.writeObject(emp);
			oos.close();
			
		≡Óõ╣ Deserialize (File ΓÁÈ Object)
		
		ObjectInputStream ois =
			new ObjectInputStream(new FileInputStream("emp.ser"));
		Employee emp = (Employee) ois.readObject();
		ois.close();
		
		≡ÓÀÊ JVM checks this marker to decide behavior.
		
82. Why default methods were introduced ? how multiple default method conflicts are resolved ?

	=>  Default methods were introduced to evolve interfaces without breaking existing code and 
		to support Java 8 features like Streams and Lambdas. Conflicts are resolved by overriding 
		the method or explicitly calling the desired interfaceΓÇÕs default implementation.
		
	Γ£õ Default methods in interfaces are optional to override because they already have an implementation.
	Γ£õ Static methods in interfaces or classes cannot be overridden; they are hidden.
	Γ£õ Abstract methods in interfaces must be implemented by concrete classes, but abstract classes are not required to implement them
	
	
83. What is Method Hiding in Java?

	=> Method hiding happens when a child class defines a static method with the same 
	   signature as a static method in the parent class.
	   
84. HashMap and ConcurrentHashMap regarding null keys and null values:
	
	=> 1∩╕Â. HashMap
		Γ£à Allows one null key
		Γ£à Allows multiple null values
		ΓÙÔ Not thread-safe
		
		Eg : HashMap<String, String> map = new HashMap<>();
		
			 map.put(null, "Hello");     // Γ£à allowed (only one null key)
			 map.put("A", null);         // Γ£à allowed
			 map.put("B", null);         // Γ£à allowed
			 
		=> Why only one null key?
			Because keys must be unique. Since null == null, only one null key is possible.
			
	=> 2∩╕Â. ConcurrentHashMap
		ΓÙÔ Does NOT allow null key
		ΓÙÔ Does NOT allow null value
		Γ£à Thread-safe
			 
		=> ConcurrentHashMap<String, String> map = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();
		
			map.put(null, "Hello");   // ΓÙÔ Throws NullPointerException
			map.put("A", null);       // ΓÙÔ Throws NullPointerException
			
	=> HashMap allows one null key and multiple null values, whereas ConcurrentHashMap does not allow any 
		null key or null value because it avoids ambiguity during concurrent access.
		

85. Key difference between get() and load()

	| Method   | Who Calls It?    | Purpose                  |
	| -------- | ---------------- | ------------------------ |
	| `get()`  | You              | Retrieve value           |
	| `load()` | Cache internally | Create value when absent |
	
	
86. Hibernate Cache Types ?

	Γ£à First-Level Cache (L1) :
		-> Enabled by default
		-> Session-level
		-> Cannot be disabled
		-> 	Not configurable
			≡ÓÀÊ No tuning required.
			
	Γ£à Second-Level Cache (L2)
		-> SessionFactory-level
		-> Shared across sessions
		-> Optional
		-> Requires provider (Ehcache, Caffeine, Infinispan, Hazelcast, etc.)
		    ≡ÓÀÊ This is what we usually tune.

	=> What Should You Cache?
		=> Not everything should be cached. Cache only:
			Γ£õ Read-mostly data
			Γ£õ Rarely updated data
			Γ£õ Small lookup/reference tables
			Γ£õ Data used frequently
			Γ£õ Data shared across users

89. How do you verify a method is called twice in Mockito?
	Γ£õ times()
			@Test
			void shouldCallMethodTwice() {
				MyService service = new MyService(dependency);

				service.process();
				service.process();

				verify(dependency, times(2)).save();
			}
			
	Γ£õ At least twice : verify(mockObject, atLeast(2)).someMethod();
	Γ£õ At most twice : verify(mockObject, atMost(2)).someMethod();
	Γ£õ Never called : verify(mockObject, never()).someMethod();

	
90. what is PowerMock and when to use it ? 
	=> We use PowerMock when normal Mockito cannot mock certain things.
		1. Static Methods
			Eg: public class Utils {
				public static String getValue() {
					return "real";
				}
			}
			
			PowerMockito.mockStatic(Utils.class);
			when(Utils.getValue()).thenReturn("mocked");

		2. Private Methods
		3. Final Classes / Final Methods (Older Mockito versions)
		
		Note : with latest version of Mockito can mock most of mocking in the above cases

93. Different OOME messages point to different root causes.

| Error Message                        | Meaning                    |
| ------------------------------------ | -------------------------- |
| `Java heap space`                    | Heap memory exhausted      |
| `GC overhead limit exceeded`         | Too much time spent in GC  |
| `Metaspace`                          | Class metadata memory full |
| `Unable to create new native thread` | OS thread limit reached    |
| `Direct buffer memory`               | NIO direct memory leak     |

	≡ÓõÓ Quick Checklist
	
	Γ£õ Identify OOME type
	Γ£õ Capture heap dump = enable heap dump and GC logging
	Γ£õ Analyze dominator tree
	Γ£õ Fix memory leak = fix code issues like unbounded collections or unclosed resources
	Γ£õ Tune JVM (last step)
	Γ£õ Add monitoring = to prevent recurrence.

94.How do you avoid performance issues caused by synchronization?

1∩╕ÂΓâú Understand Why Synchronization Hurts Performance
Synchronization can cause:
	Thread contention (threads waiting on locks)
	Context switching overhead
	Reduced parallelism
	Risk of deadlocks
	=> Goal: Minimize locking, not eliminate thread safety

2∩╕ÂΓâú Reduce Lock Scope (Most Important)
ΓÙÔ Bad (large synchronized block):
		public synchronized void process() {
		    validate();
		    calculate();
		    save();
		}	
Γ£à Good (lock only critical section):
		public void process() {
		    validate();
		    synchronized (this) {
		        calculate();
		    }
		    save();
		}
Γ£õ Less time holding lock
Γ£õ Higher throughput

3∩╕ÂΓâú Prefer Concurrent Collections
Map<String, Integer> map = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();
Why itΓÇÕs faster
	Lock striping
	Non-blocking reads
	Fine-grained locking

4∩╕ÂΓâú Use Atomic Classes Instead of synchronized
ΓÙÔ Bad
	synchronized(this) {
	    count++;
	}

Γ£à Good(lock free, Highly scalable)
AtomicInteger count = new AtomicInteger();
count.incrementAndGet();

5∩╕ÂΓâú Use Executor Framework Instead of Manual Synchronization
Γ£à Good
	ExecutorService executor = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(10);
	executor.submit(() -> process());

		Γ£õ Thread reuse
		Γ£õ Less contention
		Γ£õ Controlled concurrency
6∩╕ÂΓâú Avoid Nested Locks (Deadlock Prevention)
ΓÙÔ Bad
	synchronized(lock1) {
	    synchronized(lock2) {
	    }
	}

Γ£à Lock ordering or single lock strategy
Γ£õ Avoid deadlocks
Γ£õ Predictable performance

95. What are different ways to ensure thread safety in Java?
	=> Ensuring thread safety in Java means making sure that shared data remains consistent and correct when accessed by multiple threads 		concurrently

 1∩╕ÂΓâú Synchronization (synchronized keyword)
	=> Method-level synchronization
	=> Block-level synchronization (preferred)

 2∩╕ÂΓâú Atomic Variables (Lock-Free)
	AtomicInteger count = new AtomicInteger();
	count.incrementAndGet();

		Γ£õ Uses CAS (Compare-And-Swap)
		Γ£õ Very fast for simple operations
		ΓÙÔ Not suitable for complex logic

 3∩╕ÂΓâú Volatile Keyword (Visibility Guarantee)
	private volatile boolean running = true

		Γ£õ Guarantees visibility across threads
		ΓÙÔ Does not ensure atomicity
		
		Use when
		Single variable
		No compound operations

 4∩╕ÂΓâú Immutable Objects (Best Practice)
		public final class User {
	    private final String name;
	    private final int age;
	
	    public User(String name, int age) {
	        this.name = name;
	        this.age = age;
	    }
		}
Γ£õ No synchronization needed
Γ£õ Naturally thread-safe

 5∩╕ÂΓâú Thread-Safe Collections 
	Map<String, String> map = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();

 6∩╕ÂΓâú Executor Framework (Controlled Concurrency)
	ExecutorService executor = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(5);
	executor.submit(() -> process());

	Γ£õ Thread reuse
	Γ£õ Reduces synchronization errors

96. What is ThreadLocal and where is it used?
	=> ThreadLocal is a Java utility class that allows you to create thread-confined variablesΓÇõeach thread accessing the variable gets its 		own independent copy, even though the variable is declared as a single static or instance field
	=> ≡ÓÀÊ In simple words:
		Same variable name, different value per thread.	

	≡ÓôÔ Why do we need ThreadLocal?
			=> Without ThreadLocal, you would need:
					synchronized
					locks
					complex concurrency handling
			=> ThreadLocal solves:
					Race conditions
					Shared mutable state problems
					Performance issues from synchronization

97. Why does Hashtable not allow null keys or values?

=> Hashtable does not allow null keys or values to avoid ambiguity during retrieval and to maintain thread safety in a legacy synchronized 	design.
	Allowing null would make it impossible to distinguish between:
		-> a missing key, and
		-> a key explicitly mapped to null.

	| Feature      | Hashtable             | HashMap              |
	| ------------ | --------------------  | -------------------- |
	| Null key     | ΓÙÔ Not allowed        | Γ£õ One allowed       |
	| Null values  | ΓÙÔ Not allowed        | Γ£õ Multiple allowed  |
	| Thread-safe  | Γ£õ Yes (synchronized)  | ΓÙÔ No               |
	| Legacy class | Γ£õ Yes                 | ΓÙÔ No               |

=> Example:
		Hashtable<String, String> table = new Hashtable<>();
		table.put("A", null); // NullPointerException
		
		HashMap<String, String> map = new HashMap<>();
		map.put("A", null); // Works

=> Modern Replacement Recommendation

		ΓÙÔ Avoid using Hashtable today
		Γ£à Use:
			ConcurrentHashMap ΓÁÈ thread-safe + high performance
			Collections.synchronizedMap(new HashMap<>()) ΓÁÈ legacy-compatible
			Map<String, String> map = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();

	Note: ConcurrentHashMap also does not allow nulls ΓÇõ for similar ambiguity reasons.

98. diff between the construcotr and Setter injection :
=> Eg: Constructor Injection 
			@Component
			public class OrderService {
			
			private final PaymentService paymentService;
			
			public OrderService(PaymentService paymentService) {
				this.paymentService = paymentService;
			}
			}


	| Aspect                | Constructor Injection   | Setter Injection      |
	| --------------------- | ----------------------- | --------------------- |
	| Injection Time        | At object creation      | After object creation |
	| Dependency            | Mandatory               | Optional              |
	| Immutability          | Γ£õ Supported             | ΓÙÔ Not supported       |
	| Null Safety           | Γ£õ Guaranteed            | ΓÙÔ Risk                |
	| Testing               | Easy (constructor args) | Slightly harder       |
	| Circular Dependency   | ΓÙÔ Not allowed           | Γ£õ Possible            |
	| Recommended by Spring | Γ£õ Yes                   | ΓÙÔ Less preferred      |

99. How do you find the longest substring without repeating characters in Java?
	=> 
		String s = "ababcbb";

		        Map<Character, Integer> map = new HashMap<>();
		        int left = 0, max = 0;
		        for (int i = 0; i < s.length(); i++) {
		            char c = s.charAt(i);
		            if (map.containsKey(c)) {
		                left = Math.max(left, map.get(c) + 1);
		            }
		
		            map.put(c, i);
		            max = Math.max(max, i - left + 1);
		        }
		        System.out.println(max); //3
		        }

100. Your application throws OutOfMemoryError due to Strings. Why does this happen?
	≡Óõì Why do Strings cause OutOfMemoryError?

	1∩╕ÂΓâú Too Many String Objects Created (Most Common)
		while (true) {
	    	String s = new String("hello");
		}

	2∩╕ÂΓâú Excessive String Concatenation (+ in loops)
		String result = "";
		for (int i = 0; i < 1_000_000; i++) {
		    result += i;
		}

	3∩╕ÂΓâú String Pool Misuse (intern() abuse)
		for (int i = 0; i < 1_000_000; i++) {
	   		 String s = new String("user" + i).intern();
		}

	4∩╕ÂΓâú Reading Large Files / Responses into a String
		String data = new String(Files.readAllBytes(path));

	≡Ó¢á How to Fix String-Related OOME
		Γ£õ Use StringBuilder / StringBuffer
		Γ£õ Avoid intern() unless necessary
		Γ£õ Add eviction (LRU) to caches
		Γ£õ Stream large data instead of loading fully
		Γ£õ Remove unused references
		Γ£õ Tune heap size after fixing leaks

	≡ÓÃ» Interview-Ready Answer (Perfect)
		An OutOfMemoryError due to Strings happens when too many String objects are created or retained, often due to excessive concatenation, 
		misuse of String intern, storing Strings in long-lived collections, or loading large data into memory. Since Strings are immutable, 
		each modification creates a new object, leading to high memory usage and heap exhaustion.

101 : How would you optimize heavy string concatenation inside loops?
		=> Bad : Every time we concat It will create new object in heap
			String result = "";
			for (int i = 0; i < 1_000_000; i++) {
			    result += i;
			}

	=> Best Solution: Use  StringBuffer (Single Thread : thread safe) / StringBuilder (Multi-threaded:not thread safe) 
		=>  StringBuffer sb = new StringBuffer(); or StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(1_000_000);
			for (int i = 0; i < 1_000_000; i++) {
			    sb.append(i);
			}

102. Sorting millions of objects ΓÇõ Comparable or Comparator? Why?

	| Aspect                  | Comparable            | Comparator         |
	| ----------------------- | -------------------   | ------------------ |
	| Where logic lives       | Inside entity         | Outside entity     |
	| Method                  | `compareTo()`         | `compare()`        |
	| Flexibility             | ΓÙÔ One natural order  | Γ£õ Multiple orders  |
	| Performance             | ΓÜá∩╕Â Tightly coupled    | Γ£õ More optimizable |
	| Best for large datasets | ΓÙÔ                    | Γ£õ                  |

103. How do you avoid ConcurrentModificationException?
		=> To avoid ConcurrentModificationException, I modify collections using the iteratorΓÇÕs remove() method, use removeIf() in Java 8+, 
			or use concurrent collections like CopyOnWriteArrayList or ConcurrentHashMap in multi-threaded environments. 
			The key is not to structurally modify a collection directly while iterating over it.

104. When would you choose TreeMap over HashMap in real systems ?

	≡ÓÀÊ Choose TreeMap when you need sorted, ordered, or range-based access to keys.
		Use HashMap when you only need fast lookups with no ordering guarantees.

105. | Map Type                | Thread-Safe?     |
	 | ----------------------- | --------------   |
	 | `HashMap`               | ΓÙÔ No           |
	 | `TreeMap`               | ΓÙÔ No           |
	 | `Hashtable`             | Γ£õ Yes (legacy)  |
	 | `ConcurrentHashMap`     | Γ£õ Yes           |
	 | `ConcurrentSkipListMap` | Γ£õ Yes (sorted)  |

=> 	A TreeMap in Java is used when you need to store key-value pairs in sorted order of keys.
	Internally it uses a Red-Black Tree, so keys are automatically sorted

Eg: 1. In a gaming or competition system, players must be ranked by score.
		We can store:
			Key ΓÁÈ Score
			Value ΓÁÈ Player Name

	2. Stock Price Tracking
		In financial applications:
			Key ΓÁÈ Timestamp
			Value ΓÁÈ Stock price

106. Session management in Spring Boot

	=> In Spring Boot, session management is used to maintain user state across requests using HttpSession. 
	   By default, sessions are stored in server memory and tracked via cookies. For scalable systems, Spring Session is used with external stores like			   Redis. Spring Security also uses sessions to store authentication data, while modern microservices often use stateless JWT-based session management.

107. diff between primary and composite key? and how to define ?

	1∩╕ÂΓâú Primary Key
		≡Óõ╣ What it is
			A Primary Key (PK) is a column (or set of columns) that:
			Uniquely identifies each row in a table
			Cannot be NULL
			Is usually single-column

			Eg:	CREATE TABLE employee (
				  emp_id INT PRIMARY KEY,
				  name VARCHAR(100),
				  email VARCHAR(100)
				);

	2∩╕ÂΓâú Composite Key
		≡Óõ╣ What it is
			A Composite Key is a primary key made up of more than one column.
				≡ÓÀÊ Used when no single column is unique, but combination is unique.
				≡Óõ╣ Example
					(order_id, product_id)
					(student_id, course_id)

				Eg : CREATE TABLE order_item (
					  order_id INT,
					  product_id INT,
					  quantity INT,
					  PRIMARY KEY (order_id, product_id)
					);

	=>  Key Differences (Interview Table)
			| Aspect         | Primary Key | Composite Key              |
			| -------------- | ----------- | -------------------------- |
			| Columns        | Single      | Multiple                   |
			| Uniqueness     | One column  | Combination                |
			| Null allowed   | ΓÙÔ No        | ΓÙÔ No                    |
			| JPA annotation | `@Id`       | `@EmbeddedId` / `@IdClass` |
			| Complexity     | Simple      | More complex               |

108. Handling failures & retries without duplication (Idempotency)
	Γ£à 1. Idempotency Key (Most Common ΓÇô REST APIs) -> need to pass idempotent key in header
		Server logic
			Check if key exists
				If exists ΓÁÈ return stored response
				If not ΓÁÈ process request & store result
			Storage options
				Database
				Redis (preferred)
				Cache with TTL
	
	Γ£à 2. Database Constraints (Natural Idempotency)
			Use unique constraints to prevent duplicates.
			UNIQUE (order_id, request_id)

	Γ£à	3. Use put instead of Post wherever we can 

	Γ£à 4. Message-Based Idempotency (Kafka / MQ)
			In async systems:
				Message may be delivered more than once
				Consumer must deduplicate
					Strategy
						Store processed messageId
						Ignore duplicates

	=> Best Practices (Interview Gold)
		Γ£õ Always use Idempotency-Key for POST APIs
		Γ£õ Store result, not just the key
		Γ£õ Use TTL to avoid infinite growth
		Γ£õ Combine DB constraints + idempotency keys
		Γ£õ Make consumers idempotent in async systems

≡Óºá Interview-Ready Answer (Perfect)
		To handle failures and retries without duplication, we use idempotency. The client sends a unique idempotency key with each request, and the server 			stores and reuses the result for repeated requests instead of reprocessing. This prevents duplicate side effects during retries and is essential in 			payment, order, and distributed systems.

109. Database connection pool suddenly gets exhausted. How do you identify and fix it?
	=> When a database connection pool gets exhausted, 
		1. I first confirm it using pool metrics
		2. Then I check for unclosed connections
		3. long-running queries
		4. oversized transaction scopes
		5. I align thread pools with connection pool size
		6. enable leak detection, and analyze slow queries or thread dumps.

110. Lazy loading works locally but fails in production. WhatΓÇÕs missing?
	≡Óõ┤ Open Session In View (OSIV) difference
			Local environment ΓÁÈ OSIV enabled
			Production ΓÁÈ OSIV disabled
			OSIV keeps the Hibernate session open until the view (response) is rendered.
	
	=> Local (default behavior)
		 spring.jpa.open-in-view=true

	=> Production (best practice)  : generally in production it should disabled, and properly handle the lazy data
		spring.jpa.open-in-view=false
			Γ£õ Better performance
			Γ£õ Cleaner architecture
			ΓÙÔ Lazy loading must be handled correctly

	=> Lazy loading requires an active session, which usually means:
			@Transactional method
			Or eager fetching
			Or DTO mapping inside transaction

111. Thread-safe cache ΓÇô what will you use ?
	=>  Use ConcurrentHashMap for simple in-memory caching, 
	=>  Caffeine for production-grade, high-performance caching.
	=>  Redis : Distributed Thread-Safe Cache

112. When would you use Thread vs Runnable vs Callable in real code?
	1. Thread : Rarely Used in Real Code
		ΓÙÔ Why itΓÇÕs discouraged
			Tight coupling (task = thread)
			No return value
			No checked exception handling
			Poor scalability
			Hard to manage lifecycle

	2. Runnable ΓÇô Most Common (Fire-and-Forget) -> Logging, background cleanup, sending emails
	3. Callable ΓÇô When You Need a Result (Most Powerful) -> DB calls, External api calls.

	| Option     | Return Value | Checked Exception 	| Best Use                  |
	| ---------- | ------------ | ----------------- 	| ------------------------- |
	| `Thread`   | ΓÙÔ No         | ΓÙÔ No              | Very rare / demos         |
	| `Runnable` | ΓÙÔ No         | ΓÙÔ No              | Fire-and-forget tasks     |
	| `Callable` | Γ£õ Yes        | Γ£õ Yes             	| Tasks that return results |


113. How do you debug a production issue?

≡ÓÀÊ 1st thing I will undertsand the issue from which layer ? 
		App?
		DB?
		Network?
		External dependency?

1∩╕ÂΓâú First: Stabilize the System (Before Debugging)
	Goal: Stop the blast radius.
		Γ£õ Check severity (P0 / P1 / P2)
		Γ£õ Reduce traffic if needed (rate limiting / feature flag off)
		Γ£õ Roll back if a safe version exists
		Γ£õ Communicate status (incident channel)
	Rule: Stability first, investigation second

2∩╕ÂΓâú Understand the Symptoms (Not the Assumptions)
	Ask:
		What is failing? (API, UI, batch job)
	Since when?
		Is it intermittent or constant?
		Which users / regions / tenants?
		Any recent deployments or config changes?
	≡ÓôÔ Never assume the root cause early

3∩╕ÂΓâú Check Observability Signals (Most Important)
	≡Óõì Logs
			Error stack traces
			Correlation / request IDs
			Time patterns
	≡Óôè Metrics
			CPU, memory, GC
			DB connections
			Thread pool usage
			Latency, error rate
=> Preferred order
	Configuration change
	Feature flag off
	Rollback
	Hotfix (only if unavoidable)
	ΓÙÔ Avoid risky refactors during incidents

=> Post-Incident Actions (Interview Gold)
	Γ£õ Root Cause Analysis (RCA)
	Γ£õ Add missing logs/metrics
	Γ£õ Add alerts
	Γ£õ Write regression tests
	Γ£õ Improve runbooks

114. How do you improve performance of existing code?
	1∩╕ÂΓâú Measure First (Never Guess)
		Rule: If you canΓÇÕt measure it, you canΓÇÕt improve it.
	=> What to check
			Response time (p95 / p99)
			Throughput (RPS)
			CPU, memory, GC
			DB latency
			Thread pool usage

	2∩╕ÂΓâú Find the Real Bottleneck (80/20 Rule)
			Most performance issues come from:
				DB queries
				I/O (network, file)
				Blocking calls
				Excessive object creation
		≡ÓÀÊ Optimize the top 20% code paths that consume 80% time.

	3∩╕ÂΓâú Database Optimizations (Biggest Wins)
			Common fixes
				Γ£õ Add missing indexes
				Γ£õ Fix N+1 queries
				Γ£õ Avoid SELECT *
				Γ£õ Use pagination
				Γ£õ Reduce round trips

	4∩╕ÂΓâú Reduce Unnecessary Work
			Code-level improvements
				Remove redundant loops
				Avoid repeated calculations
				Cache expensive results
				Replace nested loops with maps/sets
				Avoid heavy logging in hot paths

116. Spring Framework vs Spring Boot:

		=> Spring MVC
		=> WebFlux
		=> Data access
		=> Transaction management
		=> Core infrastructure
	It is the foundation.

		It provides:
			=> Auto-configuration
			=> Embedded servers (Tomcat, Jetty, etc.)
			=> Starter dependencies
			=> Production-ready features (Actuator)
			=> Simplified setup
			=> Spring Boot uses a specific version of Spring Framework internally.
			
≡Óõ╣ Think of It Like This
		=> Spring Framework = Engine
		=> Spring Boot = Car built around that engine
		
		=> The engine can be upgraded even if the car model hasn't been refreshed yet.

					AOT (Ahead-of-Time compilation)

119. Explain the internal working of the Stream API pipeline. How does Lazy Evaluation work?

	=> 1∩╕Â. What Is a Stream Pipeline?
		List<String> names = List.of("John", "Jane", "Adam", "Eve");

		names.stream()
			 .filter(n -> n.startsWith("J"))
			 .map(String::toUpperCase)
			 .forEach(System.out::println);
			 
	=> Pipeline has 3 parts:
			1. Source ΓÁÈ names.stream()
			2. Intermediate operations ΓÁÈ filter(), map()
			3. Terminal operation ΓÁÈ forEach()
			=> Nothing runs until the terminal operation executes.
	
	=> Think of it like building a chain:
			=> Source ΓÁÈ FilterStage ΓÁÈ MapStage ΓÁÈ TerminalStage
			
			=> No data flows yet.
				=> This is why it is called lazy.
				
120. findFirst() returns Optional<T> because a stream may be empty, and Java avoids returning null. 
		For primitive streams, it returns specialized Optional types like OptionalInt.

		System.out.println(otp)
