233. Is ovrriding is mandatory in thread class ?
		=> Overriding run() is not mandatory when extending Thread, but if it is not overridden, 
		   the thread executes no task. When implementing Runnable, overriding run() is mandatory. 
		   To execute code in a new thread, logic must be inside run() and the thread must be started using start().


234. What is future ?
		=> A Future represents the result of an asynchronous computation.
			When you submit a task:
				Future<String> future = executor.submit(() -> {
					Thread.sleep(2000);
					return "Hello";
				});
		
				The task runs in background.
				Later, you can get result:
				String result = future.get();  // blocks until done

235. diff between submit() and execute() 
	 excute() :
		ExecutorService executor = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(2);
			executor.execute(() -> {
				System.out.println("Task running");
		});
		
		≡Óõì Key Points :
			Fire-and-forget
			No result returned
			If exception occurs ΓÁÈ printed to console
			Cannot track completion
			
	 submit() Method
			≡ÓôÔ Signatures
				Future<?> submit(Runnable task);
				Future<T> submit(Callable<T> task);
				
				Example 1 (Runnable)
				
					Future<?> future = executor.submit(() -> {
						System.out.println("Task running");
					});
					
				Example 2 (Callable)
					Future<Integer> future = executor.submit(() -> {
						return 10 + 20;
					});
	
					Integer result = future.get(); // 30

236. What happens when Kafka consumer lag increases ?
		=> Consumer lag = Number of messages produced but not yet consumed
			1. Messages Start Piling Up
			2. Increased Processing Delay (Business Impact)
			3. Risk of Data Loss (Very Important)
			4. Memory & CPU Pressure on Consumer

		=> How to Fix / Reduce Consumer Lag
			1. Increase Consumer Instances -> ≡ÓôÔ Max consumers = number of partitions
			2. Increase Topic Partitions
			3. Tune Consumer Configs -> max.poll.records=500
										fetch.min.bytes=1
										fetch.max.wait.ms=500
										enable.auto.commit=false
			4. Use Parallel Processing

237. ≡ÓõÑ What is a Retry Storm?
	=> A retry storm happens when:
			Many services retry failed requests aggressively at the same time, overwhelming a struggling downstream service even more.

	=> Imagine this architecture:
			API Gateway ΓÁÈ Order Service ΓÁÈ Payment Service ΓÁÈ DB
				Now suppose:
					Payment Service becomes slow
					It starts timing out
				
				What happens?
					Order Service retries 3 times
					API Gateway also retries
					Thousands of requests retry simultaneously
					Traffic multiplies
					Payment Service collapses completely
				
				≡ÓÈÑ This is a Retry Storm

	=> ≡Ó¢í∩╕Â How to Prevent Retry Storms
			1. Circuit Breaker Pattern
			2. Limit Retry Attempts -> Retry max 2 or 3 times
				eg:	@Retryable(maxAttempts = 3)
					public void callPaymentService() {
					}
			3. Timeout Properly -> 
			4. Rate Limiting -> Limit incoming requests when system under stress.
			5. Separate thread pools:
					Payment calls use separate pool
					So failure does not block entire system

238. Why is circuit breaker not a complete solution ?
	≡ÓõÑ First: What Circuit Breaker Actually Does :
		Circuit Breaker:
			Detects high failure rate
			Opens the circuit
			Stops calling downstream service
			After some time ΓÁÈ tries again (half-open state)
			It prevents continuous hammering of a failing service.

	=> ΓÙù Why Circuit Breaker is NOT a Complete Solution :
		1.It Only Stops Calls ΓÇõ It DoesnΓÇÕt Fix Root Cause
				If:
					DB is slow
					Thread pool is exhausted
					CPU is 100%
					Circuit breaker does not fix those.
				
				It just says:
					ΓÇ£Stop calling for now.ΓÇÙ
					Problem still exists.
		2. It Can Cause Cascading Failures Upstream => No gracefull failure
				If circuit opens:
					Order service fails
					API Gateway fails
					UI fails
					Now user sees failure.
				Without:
					Fallback
					Graceful degradation
					System still breaks.

		3. Wrong Configuration Can Make Things Worse
			If threshold is too low:
					Circuit opens too quickly (false positives)
				If threshold is too high:
					System gets hammered before opening
					So tuning matters.

239. How do you debug memory leaks in Spring Boot apps ?
	=> First: What is a Memory Leak?
			In Java:
				Memory leak = Objects are no longer needed but still referenced, so GC cannot clean them.
			In Spring Boot apps, this usually causes:
				Heap usage continuously increasing
				Frequent Full GC
				High GC pause time
				Eventually ΓÁÈ OutOfMemoryError

	=>  ≡Óºá Step-by-Step: How I Debug Memory Leaks
		1. Identify the Symptoms
			Check:
				Heap memory graph (growing continuously?)
				GC logs (Full GC frequent?)
				CPU spikes during GC?
			Tools:
				Actuator /metrics
				Prometheus + Grafana
				APM tools (New Relic, Datadog, etc.)

		2. Take a Heap Dump and Analyze Heap Dump
			=> Look for:
					Largest objects
					Retained size
					Dominator tree
					Objects growing continuously

		≡Óõì What to Check Inside Heap
			Common Spring Boot memory leak causes:
			1. Static Collections (Very Common)
					static List<User> cache = new ArrayList<>();
						=> If never cleared ΓÁÈ memory leak.

			2. Caches Without Size Limit
				Example:
					Map<String, Object> map = new HashMap<>();
					=> Without eviction ΓÁÈ grows forever.
				Solution:
					Use Caffeine
					Use Redis
					Set max size

			3. ThreadLocal Not Cleared
				In web apps:
					=> ThreadLocal<User> user = new ThreadLocal<>();

			4. Unclosed Resources
					Streams
					File handles
					DB connections
					Executors
				Always:
					Use try-with-resources
					Shutdown executors

	=> To debug memory leaks in Spring Boot, I monitor heap trends, analyze GC logs, 
	   capture heap dumps, and use tools like MAT to inspect retained objects and dominator trees. 
	   Common causes include static collections, unbounded caches, ThreadLocal misuse, and large persistence contexts.


240. If I have multiple databases and want to enable connections for them, which bean scope should I use ?
	≡ÓÀÊ Use Singleton scope (default scope).
			=> You should NOT use prototype/request/session for DataSource.

	=> ≡Óºá Why Singleton?
			In Spring Boot:
				DataSource
				EntityManagerFactory
				PlatformTransactionManager
				All are expensive objects
			They manage:
				Connection pools
				Threads
				Metadata
				DB configs

			Creating them per request would:
				Exhaust DB connections
				Kill performance
				Cause memory issues
			So they must be:
				=> @Scope("singleton")  // default
			=> But actually, you donΓÇÕt even need to specify it ΓÇõ Singleton is default.

	=> ≡ÓõÑ How Multiple Databases Are Handled  => each independntly signleton
			For multiple DBs, you define:
				Multiple DataSource beans
				Multiple EntityManagerFactory
				Multiple TransactionManager

	=> What Exactly Is a Connection Pool ?
		 A managed pool of pre-created, reusable database connections that applications borrow and return instead of creating a new connection every time.

241. Why does CPU remain normal but latency spikes?
	=> Latency is affected by waiting, not just CPU work.

		1. Thread Pool / Connection Pool Saturation (Most Common ≡ÓõÑ)
				CPU is idle, but threads are waiting.
			Examples:
				DB connection pool exhausted
				HTTP client connection pool exhausted
				Executor thread pool full
		2. Blocking I/O (DB, Network, File)
				Your threads are blocked on:
					Slow DB query
					Downstream API
					Disk I/O
				CPU isnΓÇÕt used while waiting.
		3. Lock Contention / Synchronization
			Example:
				synchronized void process() { ... }
				Only one thread executes at a time.

		4. Downstream Dependency Slowness
				If:
					DB slow
					Kafka slow
					Redis slow
					External API slow
				Your service waits ΓÁÈ latency spikes.
				CPU is not the bottleneck.

242. ≡ÓõÑ What is a Cascading Failure?
		A cascading failure happens when:
			=> Failure in one service spreads to other dependent services, eventually causing large-scale system outage.
		In short:
		≡ÓÀÊ One failure ΓÁÈ many failures

	=> ≡Óõù Example: Service Chain Failure
			API Gateway
				ΓÁô
			Order Service
				ΓÁô
			Payment Service
				ΓÁô
			Database
		Scenario:
			Database becomes slow
			Payment Service times out
			Order Service retries
			API Gateway retries
			Thread pools fill up
				Entire system becomes unresponsive
				≡ÓÈÑ Cascade complete

	=> ≡Ó¢í∩╕Â How to Prevent Cascading Failures (High-Level)
			You donΓÇÕt need full details, but mention these:
				Timeouts
				Circuit breakers
				Exponential backoff + jitter
				Bulkhead isolation
				Rate limiting
				Asynchronous communication
				Graceful degradation

243. Why do we still need abstract classes when interfaces have default methods ?
		1. Abstract Classes Can Have State (Fields)
			Abstract classes can have:
				Instance variables
				Protected fields
				Constructors
			Interfaces cannot maintain state (only public static final constants).

		2. Abstract Classes Support Constructors
			Interfaces:
				ΓÙÔ No constructors
			Abstract classes:
				Γ£õ Can enforce initialization logic

		3. Abstract Classes Allow Protected Methods
			Abstract classes:
				=> protected, package-private, private
			Interfaces:
				=> Methods are public only

		4. Abstract Classes Are Better for Code Reuse
			Abstract classes:
				Share common behavior
				Share state
				Share helper methods
			Interfaces:
				Should stay thin
				Only provide minimal default behavior

244.  How Do Threads Communicate in Java ?
		=> hreads communicate by sharing data and coordinating execution.
			There are 3 major mechanisms:
				1. wait(), notify(), notifyAll() (Classic Way)
					=> Used for inter-thread communication using object monitor (lock).
				2. Using volatile Keyword -> for visibility
				3. Blocking queue
				4. CompletableFuture

245. What are the advantages of default and static methods in interfaces ?

	=> Default methods allow us to add new functionality to interfaces without breaking existing implementations, 
	   ensuring backward compatibility. They also allow code reuse and multiple inheritance of behavior. Static methods allow defining 
	   utility methods inside interfaces, keeping related logic together and preventing overriding.

	=> what are utility methods and why static method for them ?
		They:
			Do not depend on object state
			Provide common functionality
			Are reusable across the application

			=> Because utility methods:
					DonΓÇÕt depend on instance variables
					DonΓÇÕt require object creation
					Are stateless


246. How do you design a database architecture when a Business Analyst provides requirements ?

	=> I clarify functional and non-functional requirements. Then I identify core entities and relationships and design an ER diagram. 
	   I normalize the schema to 3NF, define primary and foreign keys, and add appropriate indexes. Based on traffic and scale, 
	   I decide whether to use relational or NoSQL. Finally, 
	   I consider performance optimization, security, and scalability like partitioning or read replicas.

247. What is @Bean in Spring?
	=> @Bean is an annotation used to declare a Spring-managed bean inside a @Configuration class.
		It tells Spring:
			ΓÇ£Create this object, manage its lifecycle, and put it in the ApplicationContext.ΓÇÙ

	=>eg:   @Configuration
			public class AppConfig {
			    @Bean
			    public RestTemplate restTemplate() {
			        return new RestTemplate();
			    }
			}

248. How does @RequestBody work internally? 
	=> When a request reaches DispatcherServlet, Spring identifies the controller method. 
	   If a parameter is annotated with @RequestBody, Spring uses RequestResponseBodyMethodProcessor,
	   which relies on HttpMessageConverters like MappingJackson2HttpMessageConverter to deserialize the request body into a Java object using Jackson. 
	   If validation is present, it runs before the controller method executes

249. Explain end-to-end how Entity becomes table and SQL executes.
	=> When the application starts, Hibernate scans @Entity classes and builds metadata. If ddl-auto is enabled, it generates DDL statements and creates tables. 	   When we call repository.save(), Spring delegates to EntityManager, which uses Hibernate Session. The entity is stored in the persistence context, and 		   during transaction commit, Hibernate performs dirty checking and generates SQL, which is executed via JDBC against the database.

249. Explain Immutable objects and how to make a class immutable.
	=> An immutable object is:
		=>	An object whose state cannot be changed after it is created.
			Once constructed:
				No field can be modified
				No setter methods
				No internal data changes

	=> ≡Óºá Why Are Immutable Objects Important?
				Naturally thread-safe
				No synchronization needed
				Safe to share across threads
				Used in caching
				Used as keys in HashMap

	Eg: public final class Employee {
		    private final String name;
		    private final int age;
	   		private final List<String> skills;
	
		    public Employee(String name, int age, List<String> skills) {
		        this.name = name;
		        this.age = age;
		        this.skills = new ArrayList<>(skills);  // Defensive copy in constructor
		    }
	
		    public String getName() {
		        return name;
		    }
		
		    public int getAge() {
		        return age;
		    }
		
		    public List<String> getSkills() {
		        return Collections.unmodifiableList(skills);  // Defensive copy in getter
		    }
	}

250. What is Lock Interface and what implementaion class ?
	=> Lock is an interface in: java.util.concurrent.locks.
		=> It provides explicit locking mechanism for controlling access to shared resources in multithreaded environments.
		=> It was introduced in Java 5 as part of the concurrency utilities.

	=> Implementation Classes of Lock Interface
		=> ReentrantLock
		=> ReentrantReadWriteLock
		=> StampedLock

251. ≡ÓõÑ Cache Concurrency Strategies
		=> Very important interview topic :
				Strategy					Use Case
				READ_ONLY					Data never changes
				READ_WRITE					Read-heavy, moderate updates
				NONSTRICT_READ_WRITE		Occasional stale data allowed
				TRANSACTIONAL				Fully transactional

252. What is Lambda in Java ?
	=> A lambda expression is a way to write an anonymous function (function without name) in a shorter and cleaner way.
		=> Introduced in Java 8

	=> ΓÙÔ Problem Before Java 8
		Before Java 8, if you wanted to pass behavior (function) as a parameter, you had to:
			Create an interface
			Implement it
			Create anonymous class
			Override method
		Example (Before Java 8):
			Runnable r = new Runnable() {
			    @Override
			    public void run() {
			        System.out.println("Running");
			    }
			};
		Too much boilerplate.

	=> With Lambda (After Java 8)
		Runnable r = () -> System.out.println("Running");
		
		≡ÓõÑ Same logic.
		≡ÓõÑ 70% less code.
		≡ÓõÑ More readable.

	=> ΓÜí Does Lambda Improve Performance?

≡ÓÀÊ Short answer: Not directly because of lambda itself.
	Lambda itself does NOT magically make code faster.
		BUT it enables:
			1∩╕ÂΓâú Parallel Streams
		users.parallelStream()
		     .filter(u -> u.isActive())
		     .forEach(System.out::println);
		
		=> Now multiple threads process data.
		So performance improvement comes from:
			Streams
			Parallel processing
			Internal iteration
			Not from lambda alone.

	=> Lambda works only with Functional Interface.
		A functional interface has:
			Exactly one abstract method
		Examples:
			Runnable  -> run()
			Callable  -> call()
			Comparator -> compare()
			Comparable -> compareTo()
			Predicate -> boolean test(T t)
			Function -> R apply(T t)
			Consumer -> void accept(T t)
			Supplier -> T get()

	=> ≡ÓÃ» What If Interface Has 2 Abstract Methods?  or if it Normal fucntion
			Example:
			interface Test {
			    void a();
			    void b();
			}
			Then:
				Test t = () -> System.out.println("Hi"); ΓÙÔ
			Compiler error.
				Because lambda must match exactly one abstract method.

			Why?
			Because:
				Should lambda implement a() or b()?
			
			Ambiguity.
				Compiler cannot decide.

	=> How lambda works internally ?
		=> Lambda expressions in Java are implemented using the invokedynamic instruction introduced in Java 7. 
		   The compiler generates a synthetic private method for the lambda body, and at runtime, the JVM uses LambdaMetafactory to dynamically create an 				   implementation of the functional interface. 
		   Unlike anonymous classes, lambdas do not create separate class files, making them more memory efficient and allowing better JVM optimizations.	

	=> Can Lambda Throw Checked Exception ? : No

		List<String> list = List.of("a", "b");
			list.forEach(s -> {
			    throw new IOException();   // ΓÙÔ compile error
			});
			
		=> Why compile error?

			Because forEach expects:  Consumer<T>
			And Consumer method is:  void accept(T t);
			It does NOT declare: throws IOException

			So compiler says:
			≡ÓÀÊ "You cannot throw checked exception because method signature does not allow it."

253. How ArrayList Stores Data Internally ?
	=> Internally, ArrayList uses:
			=> transient Object[] elementData;
			≡ÓÀÊ It is just a resizable array.

	=> What Happens When You Add an Element ?
			List<Integer> list = new ArrayList<>();
			list.add(10);
			
			Internally:
				Step 1: Check Capacity
			If array is full ΓÁÈ resize.  ≡ÓÀÊ Increase by 50%
				Place element at:
					elementData[size] = newElement;
					size++
	=> Java 1.2 ΓÇô 7 -> default capacity of ArrayList is 10
		Eg: new Object[10]

	=> but in java 8 + :

		Now internally it does:
				private static final Object[] DEFAULTCAPACITY_EMPTY_ELEMENTDATA = {};
			So initially:
				≡ÓÀÊ It creates empty array of size 0
			Then when you add first element:
				ensureCapacityInternal(size + 1);
			Now it expands to:
				DEFAULT_CAPACITY = 10;
				So capacity becomes 10 on first insertion

	=> ≡ÓõÑ Special Case: If You Do
				new ArrayList<>(5);
			Now internal array is:
				new Object[5]
				It will NOT jump to 10.
				It respects your custom capacity.

	≡ÓõÑ Why ArrayList Is NOT Thread-Safe ?
		=> Because its methods like add(), remove(), get() are NOT synchronized, so multiple threads can modify internal array simultaneously, 
		   causing data corruption.

		=> so to make to ArrayList safe we can use CopyOnWriteArrayList
				Core Idea Behind CopyOnWriteArrayList
					The name itself explains it:
						=> Copy the entire array whenever a write happens.
						=> So instead of modifying the existing array,
						=> it creates a new copy and modifies that.
				=> That is why it is safe.

254. ≡ÓõÑ What Is an Indexes ?
		=> An indexes is a data structure that helps the database find rows faster without scanning the entire table.
			Without index ΓÁÈ Full table scan
			With index ΓÁÈ Fast lookup

		=> ≡ÓõÑ How Index Improves Performance
			Instead of scanning whole table, database builds a separate sorted structure.
				Most databases (MySQL, PostgreSQL, Oracle) use:

				≡ÓÀÊ B+ Tree index

		=> Suppose emails are indexed.
				Database builds:
				           [m@gmail]
				           /       \
				  [a@gmail]       [t@gmail]
				     |                |
				 row pointers      row pointers
		
		Now searching:
			WHERE email = 'c@gmail.com'
		Steps:
			1∩╕ÂΓâú Start at root
			2∩╕ÂΓâú Compare value
			3∩╕ÂΓâú Move left or right
			4∩╕ÂΓâú Reach leaf node
			5∩╕ÂΓâú Get row pointer
		Time complexity:
		≡ÓÀÊ O(log n) instead of O(n)
			ThatΓÇÕs the performance gain.

	=> ≡ÓõÑ What Happens During INSERT?
			When new row inserted:
				1∩╕ÂΓâú Find correct position in tree
				2∩╕ÂΓâú Insert into leaf node
				3∩╕ÂΓâú If node full ΓÁÈ split
				4∩╕ÂΓâú Rebalance tree
			
			This is why:
			≡ÓÀÊ Too many indexes slow down INSERT/UPDATE
				Because database must update index also.

255. How will you handle millions of records so API doesnΓÇÕt fail ?
	1. Use Pagination (Mandatory)
	2. Use Index Properly
	3. Use Batch Processing
	4. Increase DB Efficiency
		Use:
			Proper indexes
			Avoid SELECT *
			Fetch only required columns
			Avoid N+1 queries
			Use JOIN wisely
			
	5. Caching (If Data Static)
	6. Connection Pool Tuning
	7. Protect API with Limits -> Timeout configuration, Circuit breaker (Resilience4j), Graceful degradation
	8. JVM Memory Handling -> Use projection DTO instead of entity, Disable unnecessary relationships,Use fetch size
	9. Use Async Processing -> Use Kafka, Use Queue, Process async

256. Are stream introduce for improve the performace or just short way of writing code ?
	=>  Streams were NOT introduced mainly for performance.
	=>	They were introduced for functional-style programming and code readability.
	=> 	Performance improvement is a side benefit only in some cases (parallel streams)

=> How stream work Internally ?
	1. Stream Creation :
		list.stream() creates a Stream pipeline object.  and It does NOT process data immediately.
			It wraps the collectionΓÇÕs:
				Spliterator : A special iterator that can split data into multiple parts.
				Source
				Intermediate operations

	2. Pipeline Building
			Operations like:
				filter()
				map()
				sorted()
					are lazy.
			=>	They are stored as a pipeline chain.
			=>	Nothing executes yet

	3. Terminal Operation Trigger
		When toList() is called:
		≡ÓÀÊ Stream starts processing.
			It uses:
				Source ΓÁÈ filter ΓÁÈ map ΓÁÈ collect
				This is called internal iteration.
				Unlike for-loop (external iteration), stream controls iteration

=> How parallelStream() Works Step-by-Step ?
Step 1: Splitting (Fork Phase) :
		Spliterator.trySplit() divides data:
					[1..1000000]
			   ΓÁô
			[1..500000] + [500001..1000000]
			   ΓÁô
			Further split
			
			Data keeps splitting until:
				Size is small enough
				Based on CPU cores

Step 2: Task Submission :
	Each chunk is submitted as:
		ForkJoinTask
			To:
			ForkJoinPool.commonPool()

Step 3: Work Stealing
		If one thread finishes early:
			It steals work from another thread.
			This improves CPU utilization.

Step 4: Join Phase
	After all threads finish:
		Results are combined.
		This is the "Join" phase.

257. Why are parallel streams dangerous in Spring Boot ?

	=> Parallel streams use ForkJoinPool.commonPool(), which is shared globally across the JVM. 
	   In a Spring Boot application handling multiple concurrent requests, this can lead to thread contention, 
	   CPU exhaustion, and unpredictable performance. Additionally, parallel streams are not suitable for blocking operations like database or REST calls, 
	   which are common in backend services. 
	   Therefore, it is safer to use a custom ExecutorService or CompletableFuture with a dedicated thread pool 
	   for better control and scalability.

258. Popular AI Models in the Market ?
		1. OpenAI ΓÇô GPT Models -> Code generation, Chatbots, API generation
		2. Google ΓÇô Gemini  -> Multimodal (text + image + video)
		3. Anthropic ΓÇô Claude -> Long context handling, 
		4. Meta ΓÇô LLaMA -> 
		5. Microsoft ΓÇô Copilot -> Code auto-completion, Test case generation

=> How does an LLM search and give results ?
	1. LLMs do not search like traditional search engines. They are trained on massive datasets to learn statistical relationships between words. 
	2. When given input, the text is tokenized and converted into vectors. Using transformer architecture and self-attention mechanisms, the model predicts the         next most probable token repeatedly until the response is generated. 
	3. If connected to external systems using RAG(Retrieval-Augmented Generation), the model can retrieve real-time data before generating output.

259. What is Cache ?
	=> A fast temporary storage layer to avoid repeated expensive operations (DB calls, API calls)
	=> There are two main types used in Spring Boot:
			Γ£à In-Memory Cache (like ConcurrentHashMap, Caffeine)
			Γ£à Distributed Cache (like Redis)

	=> How Data is Stored in Cache?
		Case 1: In-Memory Cache (Inside JVM)
			Example: Spring Boot default cache or Caffeine

			Internally it uses: ConcurrentHashMap<K, V>
			=> So data is stored as: Key ΓÁÈ Value  Eg: "USER_101" ΓÁÈ User Object

		So it is NOT : List, JSON, Text
		Java objects directly in heap memory

		Case 2: Redis (Distributed Cache)  -> Uses the RAM of the machine where Redis is installed
		Redis stores data as: Key ΓÁÈ Value
		But value can be :String, JSON, Hash, List, Set, Sorted Set, Bitmap, HyperLogLog

		Example:
		Key: user:101
		Value: {"id":101,"name":"Roy","active":true}

260. ≡Óõ╖ What is a Connection Pool ?
		=> A Connection Pool is a cache of reusable database connections.
		=> Instead of:
			=> Opening a new DB connection for every request ΓÙÔ (very slow)
			=> Closing it immediately ΓÙÔ
		We:
			=> Create a pool of connections at startup Γ£à
			=> Reuse them for multiple requests Γ£à

	=> Why Do We Need Connection Pool?
		Creating a DB connection is expensive because:
			TCP handshake
			Authentication
			Session creation
			Memory allocation
			DB process/thread allocation
		
		If you create connection per request:
			1000 users ΓÁÈ 1000 connection creations ΓÁÈ DB crash ≡ÓõÑ
		With pool:
			1000 users ΓÁÈ reuse 20ΓÇô50 connections efficiently Γ£à

=> 1∩╕ÂΓâú Application Starts
		Connection Pool creates N database connections
			Stores them in an internal data structure (usually a queue)
		Example:
			Initial Pool Size = 10
		=> 	Pool now has 10 ready-to-use connections.

=> Internally What Data Structure Is Used : Blocking Queue

=> Most Popular: HikariCP
		Spring Boot uses:
			≡ÓÀÊ HikariCP
		It is:
			Very fast
			Lightweight
			Low latency
			Production ready

=> How To Create Connection Pool?
≡Óõ╣ In Spring Boot (Recommended Way)
			You donΓÇÕt manually create it.
		Just add:
			spring.datasource.url=jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/testdb
			spring.datasource.username=root
			spring.datasource.password=root
			spring.datasource.hikari.maximum-pool-size=20
			spring.datasource.hikari.minimum-idle=5
			spring.datasource.hikari.idle-timeout=30000
			spring.datasource.hikari.max-lifetime=1800000
	=> 	Spring Boot automatically configures HikariCP.

 => How is it different from Thread Pool ?	
	| Thread Pool     | Connection Pool        |
	| --------------- | ---------------------- |
	| Manages threads | Manages DB connections |
	| CPU resource    | External DB resource   |


261. Can Lambda throw an exception ?
		=> Yes, a lambda can throw exceptions. If it is an unchecked exception, there is no restriction. 
		   But for checked exceptions, the functional interface method must declare the exception in its throws clause. 
		   Since most standard functional interfaces like Consumer and Function do not declare checked exceptions, 
		   we usually handle them using try-catch inside the lambda or wrap them in RuntimeException

Eg 1:   @FunctionalInterface
		public interface Consumer<T> {
		    void accept(T t);   // No "throws"
		}
		
	=>	Since accept() does not declare throws IOException,
	=>	the lambda cannot throw checked exception.

Eg 2:   @FunctionalInterface
		interface MyInterface {
		    void process() throws IOException;
		}
		
		Then:
			MyInterface m = () -> {
			    throw new IOException("Error");
			};
		This works Γ£õ

262. What Is a Custom Exception ?
	=> A custom exception is a user-defined exception class that extends:
			RuntimeException (Unchecked) Γ£à recommended for Spring apps
		OR
			Exception (Checked)

=> How To Create Custom Exception ? : In modern Spring Boot apps, we usually extend RuntimeException.
	Eg : public class ResourceNotFoundException extends RuntimeException {

		    public ResourceNotFoundException(String message) {
		        super(message);
		    }
		
		    public ResourceNotFoundException(String message, Throwable cause) {
		        super(message, cause);
		    }
		}

		ΓÙÔ Checked Custom Exception (Less Common in Spring)
				public class InvalidAmountException extends Exception {
				
				    public InvalidAmountException(String message) {
				        super(message);
				    }
				}
				
				Then method must declare:

	=> From Where Should We Throw Custom Exception ?
		Γ£õ From Service Layer (Best Practice)
		 Example:
			public User getUser(Long id) {
			    return userRepository.findById(id)
			            .orElseThrow(() -> new ResourceNotFoundException("User not found"));
			}
			
			Why service layer?
				Business validation belongs here

	=> Can We Throw Custom Exception From Anywhere?
			Technically Γ£à YES
			You can throw from:
				Controller
				Service
				Repository
				Utility class
				Even inside lambda
		Example:
			throw new ResourceNotFoundException("Invalid ID");

=> What Happens After Throwing ?
	In Spring Boot, we handle exceptions using:

		@RestControllerAdvice
		public class GlobalExceptionHandler {
		
		    @ExceptionHandler(ResourceNotFoundException.class)  // to handle specific exception 
		    public ResponseEntity<String> handle(ResourceNotFoundException ex) {
		        return ResponseEntity.status(HttpStatus.NOT_FOUND)
		                             .body(ex.getMessage());
		    }

			@ExceptionHandler(Exception.class) // to handle any kind of exception
				public ResponseEntity<String> handleAll(Exception ex) {
					return ResponseEntity
							.status(HttpStatus.INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR)
							.body("Something went wrong");
			}
		}
		
		This gives clean API response instead of stack trace.

263. How does application read application.yml?
	How does it know where to read values from?
	How does @Value or config class get those values?

1. Who Reads application.yml?
	Spring Boot automatically reads configuration files during startup using,
	Internally, Spring Boot uses:
		SpringApplication
		Environment
		PropertySources
		ConfigDataEnvironment

2. What Happens During Application Startup ?
	When you run:
		SpringApplication.run(MyApplication.class, args);
		
		Spring Boot does this:
			Step 1: Bootstrap Phase
				It looks for config files in default locations:
					classpath:/application.yml
					classpath:/application.properties
					file:./config/
					file:./
				Priority order matters.
	Internally this .yml file or application.properties file will converted into key:value pair
	then Stored inside:
			Environment ΓÁÈ PropertySources ΓÁÈ Map  (Spring maintains: MutablePropertySources)

	=> How Does @Value Read It ?
			@Value("${server.port}")
			private int port;
			
			What happens?
				1. Spring creates bean
				2. It sees ${server.port}
				3. It asks Environment
				3. Environment looks into PropertySources
				4. Finds key
				5. Injects value
	
	=> How Does @ConfigurationProperties Work ?

	Example:
		app:
		  name: MyApp
		  timeout: 5000
		
		Java class:
		@ConfigurationProperties(prefix = "app")
		@Component
		public class AppConfig {
		    private String name;
		    private int timeout;
		}
		
		How it works internally:
			Spring Binder API maps properties
			Uses reflection
			Matches prefix
			Sets fields automatically

	=> How To Read Property Manually ?
		@Autowired
		private Environment env;
		
		public void print() {
		    String port = env.getProperty("server.port");
		}

	=> During application startup, Spring Boot uses SpringApplication to create and prepare an Environment object. 
	   It loads configuration files like application.yml from predefined locations using ConfigDataEnvironmentPostProcessor. 
	   YAML is parsed into key-value pairs and stored inside PropertySources. When we use @Value or @ConfigurationProperties, 
	   Spring resolves the property from the Environment and injects it into the bean using the Binder API

	=> What Happens If Property Not Found ?
		≡ÓÓó Case 1: Using @Value
				@Value("${app.name}")
				private String appName;
				ΓÙÔ If app.name is NOT present:
					Application fails at startup with:  error : Could not resolve placeholder 'app.name'
						
		≡ÓÓó Case 2: Using @ConfigurationProperties
				@ConfigurationProperties(prefix = "app")
				public class AppConfig {
				    private String name;
				}
				If app.name is missing:
					Γ£õ No exception
					Γ£õ Field remains null

		≡ÓÓó Case 3: Using Environment.getProperty()
				env.getProperty("app.name");
					If property missing:
						Γ£õ Returns null
						Γ£õ No exception

	=> How To Provide Default Value ?
		Γ£à Method 1: Default Value in @Value
				Most common:
					@Value("${app.name:DefaultApp}")
					private String appName;
				
				If app.name not present:
					Γ£õ appName = "DefaultApp"
					This is safest way.

		Γ£à Method 2: Default in Environment
			env.getProperty("app.name", "DefaultApp");

		Γ£à Method 3: Default in @ConfigurationProperties
			Just initialize field:
				private String name = "DefaultApp";
				If property missing ΓÁÈ default used.

I also ensure APIs are stateless, versioned, and well-documented

265. Where do we validate username/password?
	 Who validates it ΓÇõ us or Spring Security?
	 Where do we write JWT?
	 Which component actually validates things?

≡ÓÓó PHASE 1 ΓÇõ Username/Password Validation (Login) :
	Step 1: Client Sends Login Request
		POST /login
		{
		  "username": "john",
		  "password": "1234"
		}

	Step 2: Who Validates It?
		Spring Security does NOT automatically validate against DB.
		
		It uses these components internally:
			UsernamePasswordAuthenticationFilter
			        ΓÁô
			AuthenticationManager
			        ΓÁô
			AuthenticationProvider
			        ΓÁô
			UserDetailsService

	1∩╕ÂΓâú UsernamePasswordAuthenticationFilter :
			This filter:
				=> Reads username/password from request
				=> Creates Authentication object
				=> Sends it to AuthenticationManager

	2∩╕ÂΓâú AuthenticationManager
				This is the main interface:
				Authentication authenticate(Authentication auth);
				It delegates to:

	3∩╕ÂΓâú AuthenticationProvider
				Default implementation:
					DaoAuthenticationProvider
					This is where actual validation happens.

	4∩╕ÂΓâú UserDetailsService (YOU IMPLEMENT THIS) :
				Here YOU fetch user from DB:
					@Service
					public class CustomUserDetailsService implements UserDetailsService {
					
					    @Override
					    public UserDetails loadUserByUsername(String username) {
					        return userRepository.findByUsername(username)
					                .orElseThrow(() -> new UsernameNotFoundException("User not found"));
					    }
					}
					
					Spring Security then:
						Compares password using PasswordEncoder
						If match ΓÁÈ Authentication success
						If not ΓÁÈ 401
					So:
						Γ£õ You fetch user
						Γ£õ Spring Security validates password

≡ÓÓó PHASE 2 ΓÇõ JWT Creation
		After successful authentication: You manually generate JWT.
		Example:
			String token = jwtUtil.generateToken(username);
		
		This is usually done in:
			Authentication controller
			Or custom success handler

	=> Where Do We Write JWT Code ?
		You create a utility class:
			@Component
			public class JwtUtil {
			    public String generateToken(String username) {
			        // create token using secret key
			    }
			}

≡ÓÓó PHASE 3 ΓÇõ JWT Validation for Every Request
	After login:
		Client sends:
			Authorization: Bearer eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9...
		Now who validates JWT ?
			You must create:
				Custom JWT Filter
			Usually extends:
				OncePerRequestFilter
			
			Example:
			public class JwtAuthenticationFilter extends OncePerRequestFilter {

	This filter:
		Extracts token from header
		Validates using JwtUtil
		Sets Authentication in SecurityContext

≡ÓõÑ Complete Flow Diagram :
			Login Request
			   ΓÁô
			UsernamePasswordAuthenticationFilter
			   ΓÁô
			AuthenticationManager
			   ΓÁô
			DaoAuthenticationProvider
			   ΓÁô
			UserDetailsService (DB call)
			   ΓÁô
			PasswordEncoder.matches()
			   ΓÁô
			JWT Generated
			-----------------------------------
			Subsequent Request
			   ΓÁô
			JwtAuthenticationFilter
			   ΓÁô
			Validate Token
			   ΓÁô
			Set Authentication in SecurityContext
			   ΓÁô
			Controller

=> If you want to Role based Authentication we need to create Security Configuration class
		@Configuration
		@EnableMethodSecurity
		public class SecurityConfig {
		    @Bean
		    public SecurityFilterChain securityFilterChain(HttpSecurity http) throws Exception {
		        http
		            .csrf(csrf -> csrf.disable())
		            .authorizeHttpRequests(auth -> auth
		                .requestMatchers("/admin/**").hasRole("ADMIN")
		                .requestMatchers("/user/**").hasAnyRole("USER", "ADMIN")
		                .anyRequest().authenticated()
		            )
		            .formLogin();
		        return http.build();
		    }
		}


266. What Is an API Contract ?
	=> An API contract is a formal agreement between:
			Backend (API provider)
			        ΓÁõ
			Client (Frontend / Mobile / Other Service)

	=> It defines:
			What endpoints exist
			What request format should be
			What response format will be
			What status codes are returned
			What authentication is required

			It is basically:
			≡Óôã The specification of how client and server communicate.

	=> Why Is API Contract Important ?
		 Because client and backend are developed independently.
				=> So contract ensures:
					Γ£õ Stability
					Γ£õ Clear expectations
					Γ£õ No unexpected breaking changes
					Γ£õ Parallel development

267. Status codes and meaning :
	Code 	Constant 					(Example)				Message	Description
	200		SC_OK						OK						The request was successful.
	201		SC_CREATED					Created					A new resource was successfully created (common for POST requests).
	204		SC_NO_CONTENT				No Content				The request was successful, but no response body is returned (common for DELETE operations).
	400		SC_BAD_REQUEST				Bad Request				The server couldn't understand the request due to invalid syntax or missing parameters.
	401		SC_UNAUTHORIZED				Unauthorized			Authentication is required and has failed or not been provided.
	403		SC_FORBIDDEN				Forbidden				The client is authenticated but does not have permission to access the resource.
	404		SC_NOT_FOUND				Not Found				The requested resource could not be found on the server.
	405		SC_METHOD_NOT_ALLOWED		Method Not Allowed		The HTTP method used is not supported for the requested resource.
	409		SC_CONFLICT					Conflict				The request could not be completed due to a conflict with the current state of the resource 																	(e.g., creating a resource that already exists).
	500		SC_INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR	Internal Server Error	A generic error message when an unexpected condition was encountered on the server.
	503		SC_SERVICE_UNAVAILABLE		Service Unavailable		The server is temporarily unable to handle the request, often due to maintenance or overload.


268. how to handle api slowness ? what we will do to faster ?
	≡Óõ╖ Step 1: Identify Where Slowness Is
			API slowness usually comes from:
				Database
				External API calls
				Large payload
				CPU-heavy processing
				Network latency
				Thread blocking
				Connection pool exhaustion
		=> You must profile before fixing.

	1∩╕ÂΓâú Database Optimization (Most Common Cause) :
			Γ£à Add Indexes
			Γ£à Avoid N+1 Problem (Very Common in JPA)
			Γ£à Use Pagination
			Γ£à Optimize Query -> avoid select *

	2∩╕ÂΓâú Use Caching (Very Powerful) :
	3∩╕ÂΓâú Connection Pool Tuning -> based on request that call set a pool size in properties file
	4∩╕ÂΓâú Use Asynchronous Processing 
			Use @Async
			Use CompletableFuture
			Use messaging (Kafka / RabbitMQ)
	5∩╕ÂΓâú Reduce Payload Size -> use DTO
	7∩╕ÂΓâú Avoid Blocking Calls -> use webclient instead of feignclient
	8∩╕ÂΓâú Add Timeout for External Services
	9∩╕ÂΓâú Horizontal Scaling and vertical scaling in server

269. how to implement pagination properly ? what is Pageable ?
	≡Óõ╖ What is Pageable? 
		Pageable is an Interface in Spring Data that represents:
			Page number
			Page size
			Sorting
		It belongs to:
			≡ÓÀÊ Spring Data JPA

	Γ£à Step 1: Repository
			public interface UserRepository extends JpaRepository<User, Long> {
			    Page<User> findAll(Pageable pageable);
			}
			=> Notice return type: Page<User>

	Γ£à Step 2: Service Layer
			public Page<User> getUsers(Pageable pageable) {
			    return userRepository.findAll(pageable);
			}

	Γ£à Step 3: Controller
			@GetMapping("/users")
			public Page<User> getUsers(
			        @RequestParam(defaultValue = "0") int page,
			        @RequestParam(defaultValue = "10") int size,
			        @RequestParam(defaultValue = "id") String sortBy) {
			
			    Pageable pageable = PageRequest.of(page, size, Sort.by(sortBy));
			
			    return service.getUsers(pageable);
			}

	=> GET /users?page=0&size=5&sortBy=name

	≡Óõ╖ What is Page?
			Page<T> contains:
				content (actual data)
				totalElements
				totalPages
				currentPage
				size
				isFirst
				isLast

270. What is the difference between @PathVariable and @RequestParam ? and  Where exactly do we use each?

	=> 1∩╕ÂΓâú What is @PathVariable?
				@PathVariable is used to capture values from the URL path.
				It represents a specific resource.
				
			Γ£à Example
				@GetMapping("/users/{id}")
				public User getUser(@PathVariable Long id) {
				    return service.getUser(id);
				}
				
				Request:  GET /users/10
	
		Use it when:
			Γ£õ Fetching specific resource
			Γ£õ Updating specific resource
			Γ£õ Deleting specific resource

	=> 2∩╕ÂΓâú What is @RequestParam ?
		@RequestParam is used to capture values from the query string.
			It represents filtering, sorting, optional data, pagination, etc.
		Γ£à Example
			@GetMapping("/users")
			public List<User> getUsers(
			        @RequestParam int page,
			        @RequestParam int size) {
			
			    return service.getUsers(page, size);
			}
			Request:  GET /users?page=0&size=10
		

271. What is the difference between PUT and PATCH ?
	=> 1∩╕ÂΓâú PUT ΓÇõ Full Update
		≡ÓÀÊ PUT is used to update the entire resource.
			If you send PUT request, you are saying:
				ΓÇ£Replace this resource completely with this new data.ΓÇÙ

	Note : After PUT ΓÁÈ Entire record replaced. if you miss any field that field becom null in DB

	=> 2∩╕ÂΓâú PATCH ΓÇõ Partial Update
		≡ÓÀÊ PATCH is used to update only specific fields.
		You are saying:
			ΓÇ£Update only these fields, keep rest unchanged.ΓÇÙ

	Note : Only provided fields changed.
		   Others remain unchanged.

	=> ≡Óõ╖ Important Rule
			PATCH updates only fields present in request body.
			PUT updates entire resource.


272. Difference between HashMap and TreeMap ? When to use which ?

	| Feature         | HashMap                  | TreeMap                       |
	| --------------- | ----------------------   | ----------------------------- |
	| Order           | ΓÙÔ No order             | Γ£à Sorted order                |
	| Data Structure  | Hash Table               | Red-Black Tree                |
	| Time Complexity | O(1) average             | O(log n)                      |
	| Null Key        | Γ£à One null key allowed | ΓÙÔ Not allowed                 |
	| Performance     | Faster                   | Slower than HashMap           |
	| Sorting         | ΓÙÔ No                   | Γ£à Natural / Custom Comparator |


	=> Γ£à When To Use HashMap
			Γ£õ When order doesnΓÇÕt matter
			Γ£õ Need high performance
			Γ£õ Most common usage
			Γ£õ Caching
			Γ£õ Storing lookup data
		Example:
			Session storage
			User ID ΓÁÈ User object mapping

	=> Γ£à When To Use TreeMap
			Γ£õ When sorted data required
			Γ£õ Range queries needed
			Γ£õ Finding closest key
			Γ£õ Floor / Ceiling operations
			
			Example:
				Leaderboard sorted by score
				Price-based sorting
				Time-based event sorting

	=> Γ£à What Exactly Stored in Heap ?
			Γ£õ Objects
			Γ£õ Instance variables
			Γ£õ Arrays
			Γ£õ String objects (not literals pool explanation below)
			Γ£õ Static variables (important interview point)
			Γ£õ Runtime constant pool references

	=> Γ£à What Exactly Stored in Stack ?
			Γ£õ Local variables
			Γ£õ Method parameters
			Γ£õ Reference variables
			Γ£õ Return addresses
			Γ£õ Partial results

	=> Γ£à What Stored in Metaspace ?
			Γ£õ Class definitions
			Γ£õ Method metadata
			Γ£õ Field metadata
			Γ£õ Static method info
			Γ£õ Bytecode
			Γ£õ Runtime constant pool

275. What is Concurrency API ?
	=> Java Concurrency API is a set of classes and utilities that help us:
	=> Write multi-threaded programs safely and efficiently.

	≡Óõ╖ Why Do We Need Concurrency API?
			If we create threads manually:
				new Thread(() -> {}).start();
			Problems:
				ΓÙÔ Hard to manage
				ΓÙÔ Hard to control thread lifecycle
				ΓÙÔ No pooling
				ΓÙÔ No scheduling
				ΓÙÔ Complex synchronization
			Concurrency API solves this.

	≡Óõ╖ Main Components of Concurrency API

		≡ÓÓó 1∩╕ÂΓâú Executor Framework :
				Most important.
					Instead of creating threads manually:
				We use:
					ExecutorService executor = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(5);
				Purpose:
					Γ£õ Thread pooling
					Γ£õ Better resource management
					Γ£õ Reuse threads
					Γ£õ Control concurrency

		≡ÓÓó 2∩╕ÂΓâú Future :
				Used to get result from async task.
					Future<Integer> future = executor.submit(() -> 10 + 20);
					Integer result = future.get(); // blocks
				Purpose:
					Γ£õ Get async result
					Γ£õ Check if task completed
					Γ£õ Cancel task

		≡ÓÓó 3∩╕ÂΓâú CompletableFuture (Very Powerful)
				Used for:
					Γ£õ Non-blocking async programming
					Γ£õ Chaining tasks
					Γ£õ Combining multiple async calls
				
				Example:
					CompletableFuture.supplyAsync(() -> "Hello")
					    .thenApply(s -> s + " World")
					    .thenAccept(System.out::println);
					
					Very common in microservices.

		≡ÓÓó 4∩╕ÂΓâú Concurrent Collections
				Thread-safe collections:
					Class					Purpose
					ConcurrentHashMap		Thread-safe HashMap
					CopyOnWriteArrayList	Thread-safe List
					BlockingQueue			Producer-consumer pattern

		≡ÓÓó 5∩╕ÂΓâú Locks (Advanced Synchronization)
				Instead of synchronized, we use:
					ReentrantLock lock = new ReentrantLock();
				Advantages:
					Γ£õ More flexible
					Γ£õ tryLock()
					Γ£õ Fair locking


276. How to call a stored procedure from JPA / Spring Boot ?
	=> There are 3 main ways to call stored procedures in JPA.

		1. Using @Procedure (Simple Way ΓÇô Spring Data JPA) :
				public interface EmployeeRepository extends JpaRepository<Employee, Long> {
				    @Procedure(name = "get_employees_by_dept")
				    List<Employee> getEmployeesByDept(@Param("dept_name") String deptName);
				}

		2. Using @NamedStoredProcedureQuery (Entity-Level Mapping) 
		3. Using EntityManager (Most Flexible & Professional)

277. What is JPA Specification ?
	=> JPA Specification is a way to build dynamic queries programmatically using the Criteria API.
		It allows you to:
			Γ£õ Build queries dynamically
			Γ£õ Add conditions based on input
			Γ£õ Avoid writing multiple custom queries
			Γ£õ Keep code clean and maintainable

	=> ≡Óõ╖ Step-by-Step Example
	Γ£à Step 1: Add JpaSpecificationExecutor
		Eg : public interface EmployeeRepository extends JpaRepository<Employee, Long>, JpaSpecificationExecutor<Employee> {}
				-> Now repository supports Specification.

	Γ£à Step 2: Create Specification :
		public class EmployeeSpecification {
		
		    public static Specification<Employee> hasAgeGreaterThan(int age) {
		        return (root, query, criteriaBuilder) ->
		                criteriaBuilder.greaterThan(root.get("age"), age);
		    }
		
		    public static Specification<Employee> hasDepartment(String dept) {
		        return (root, query, criteriaBuilder) ->
		                criteriaBuilder.equal(root.get("department"), dept);
		    }
		
		    public static Specification<Employee> hasSalaryGreaterThan(double salary) {
		        return (root, query, criteriaBuilder) ->
		                criteriaBuilder.greaterThan(root.get("salary"), salary);
		    }
		}

	Γ£à Step 3: Combine Specifications :

		Specification<Employee> spec = Specification
		        .where(EmployeeSpecification.hasAgeGreaterThan(25))
		        .and(EmployeeSpecification.hasDepartment("IT"))
		        .and(EmployeeSpecification.hasSalaryGreaterThan(50000));
		
		List<Employee> employees = repository.findAll(spec);

≡ÓõÑ Generated SQL (Internally)
		SELECT *
		FROM employee
		WHERE age > 25
		AND department = 'IT'
		AND salary > 50000;

	=>	HashMap collision handling -> collision
	=>	Browser history navigation -> backword, forward

279. What You Should Know About Pipelines ?
		1. What is a Pipeline?
			A CI/CD pipeline is an automated workflow that:
				Developer Code ΓÁÈ Build ΓÁÈ Test ΓÁÈ Package ΓÁÈ Deploy
				It ensures every code change is automatically tested and deployed safely.
		=>	Example flow:
				Git Commit
				   ΓÁô
				Build (Maven / Gradle)       -> mvn clean compile
				   ΓÁô
				Unit Tests                   -> Run all test cases : mvn test
				   ΓÁô						 -> Run a specific test class : mvn -Dtest=TestClassName test
				Code Quality (SonarQube)	 -> Run specific test methods : mvn -Dtest=TestClassName#methodName test	
				   ΓÁô
				Build Artifact (JAR / Docker Image)
				   ΓÁô
				Deploy to Dev / QA / Prod

280. Explain the main method in Java ?

	=> The main() method is the entry point of a Java application.
	   When the JVM starts execution, it looks for the main method and begins running the program from there.

	=> Syntax Breakdown :
	1. public : 
		=> The JVM must be able to access the method from anywhere.
		=> If it is not public: 
				JVM cannot access it ΓÁÈ Program will not run.

	2. static :
		=> main() must be static because JVM calls it without creating an object.
		=> if not : new Test().main() -> But JVM does not create objects automatically. So it must be static.

	3. void :
		=> It means main method does not return any value.
		=> The JVM does not expect any return value from the main method.

	4. main :
		=> This is the method name recognized by JVM as the starting point.
		If you rename:
			eg:	public static void start(String[] args)
			=> Program wonΓÇÕt run.

	5. String[] args :
		=> This allows command line arguments to be passed.
			Example:
				java Test hello world
			Then:
				args[0] = hello
				args[1] = world

			eg:	 for(String s : args){
		            System.out.println(s);
		         }

		=> Can We Overload main() ?  : Yes
		=> But JVM always starts with : main(String[] args)

		=> Can We Change args Name ? 
			Yes.
				public static void main(String[] abc)
					(or)
				public static void main(String... args)
					Both are valid.

		=> Can main method be private? : No
		=> Can main method be final? : Yes
		=> Can main method be synchronized? : Yes
		=> Can main method throw exception? : Yes
		=> Can we run a Java program without the main method ?
			  -> You cannot execute Java code without main() in modern JVM.

				Java Version			Static Block Runs Without main()?			Reason												
				Java 6 or earlier		Γ£à Yes										Class loaded before main check
				Java 7+ (modern)		ΓÙÔ No										JVM validates main() first

281. What is a Red-Black Tree ?

		=> A Red-Black Tree is a self-balancing binary search tree where each node is either red or black. 
		   It maintains balance using a set of properties such as the root being black, no two red nodes appearing consecutively, and all root-to-leaf paths 			   having the same number of black nodes. When violations occur during insertion or deletion, the tree uses recoloring and rotations to restore balance. 		   This ensures search, insertion, and deletion operations run in O(log n) time. In Java, Red-Black Trees are used internally in TreeMap, TreeSet, and 		   	   also in HashMap for handling large collision buckets.

282. Describe the concept fucntional programming ?
	=> Functional programming focuses on what to do rather than how to do it,
	=> Core Concepts of Functional Programming :

		1. Pure Functions :
			-> A pure function always produces the same output for the same input and does not modify external state.
					Example:
						int add(int a, int b) {
						    return a + b;
						}
					Properties:
						No side effects
						Deterministic
						Easy to test

		2. Immutability : This avoids bugs in multithreaded environments.
			-> Functional programming encourages immutable data.
					Once created, the value cannot change.
				Example:
					final int x = 10;
						Instead of modifying data, FP creates new values.
				Example:
						Old List ΓÁÈ New List

		3. First-Class Functions :
			-> Functions can be:
					Assigned to variables
					Passed as parameters
					Returned from methods
					Example using lambda expression:
							Function<Integer, Integer> square = x -> x * x;
							System.out.println(square.apply(5));

		4. Higher-Order Functions :
			-> A higher-order function is a function that:
					Takes another function as input
						(or)
					Returns a function
						Example using Streams API:

		5. Lambda Expressions
				Lambda expressions allow writing short inline functions.

283. what is @PostConstruct and @PreDestroy
	=> 1∩╕ÂΓâú @PostConstruct
			This method runs after the bean is created and dependencies are injected.

			Example:
				import jakarta.annotation.PostConstruct;
				import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;
				
				@Component
				public class MyService {
				
				    @PostConstruct
				    public void init() {
				        System.out.println("Bean initialized");
				    }
				}

			=>	Lifecycle
					Bean created
					ΓÁô
					Dependencies injected
					ΓÁô
					@PostConstruct executed
					ΓÁô
					Bean ready to use
				
				Use cases:
					Load configuration
					Initialize cache
					Open connections
					Prepare resources

	=> 2∩╕ÂΓâú @PreDestroy
			Runs before the bean is destroyed.
				Example:
				import jakarta.annotation.PreDestroy;
				import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;
				
				@Component
				public class MyService {
				
				    @PreDestroy
				    public void cleanup() {
				        System.out.println("Bean is about to be destroyed");
				    }
				}
				Lifecycle
					Application shutting down
						ΓÁô
					@PreDestroy executed
						ΓÁô
					Bean destroyed
				
				Use cases:
					Close DB connections
					Close files
					Cleanup resources

	=>  | Method         | When Called                |
		| -------------- | -------------------------- |
		| Constructor    | Object creation            |
		| @PostConstruct | After dependency injection |
		| @PreDestroy    | Before bean destruction    |

284. How to handle concurrent transactions without loosing data ?
		1. Database Transactions :
			Use ACID properties.
					A ΓÁÈ Atomicity -> All operations succeed or none
					C ΓÁÈ Consistency -> Database remains valid
					I ΓÁÈ Isolation -> Transactions do not interfere
					D ΓÁÈ Durability -> Changes persist
			=>	In Spring Boot:
						@Transactional
						public void transferMoney(){
						}
			=>	This ensures the transaction is executed safely.

		2. Isolation Levels :
			Isolation levels control how concurrent transactions interact.
				Isolation Level					Problem Prevented
				READ_UNCOMMITTED				nothing
				READ_COMMITTED					dirty reads
				REPEATABLE_READ					non-repeatable reads
				SERIALIZABLE					all concurrency issues
			Example:
				@Transactional(isolation = Isolation.SERIALIZABLE)

	3. Optimistic Locking :
		=>	Assumes conflicts are rare.
				We add a version column.
			Example table:
				id | balance | version
				JPA Entity:
					@Entity
					public class Account {
					    @Id
					    private Long id;
					    private double balance;
					    @Version
					    private Long version;
					}
					
				How it works:
				
					User A reads version = 1
					User B reads version = 1
						User A updates ΓÁÈ version becomes 2
						User B tries update ΓÁÈ version mismatch ΓÙÔ
				
				Spring throws:
					OptimisticLockException

		4. Pessimistic Locking :
				Here the database locks the row so other transactions cannot update it.
					Example:
						@Lock(LockModeType.PESSIMISTIC_WRITE)
						Account findById(Long id);
					This ensures:
						Transaction 1 locks row
						Transaction 2 must wait

	=> Use locking, isolation levels, and optimistic concurrency to manage concurrent transactions effectively.
			1. Implement optimistic locking using versioning to prevent lost updates.
			2. Use pessimistic locking to lock records during a transaction.
			3. Set appropriate isolation levels (e.g., READ_COMMITTED) to control visibility of changes.
			4. Utilize database transactions to ensure atomicity and consistency.

285. How to avoid same multiple POST requests ?
		1. Best Solution: Idempotency Key (Industry Standard)
			Most payment systems (Stripe, PayPal) use this.
			Client sends a unique key with the request.
		Example request:
				POST /payments
				Idempotency-Key: 12345
		Server logic:
				Check if key already exists
				If yes ΓÁÈ return previous response
				If no ΓÁÈ process request and store result

		2. 2. Database Unique Constraint
				Example:
					transaction_id UNIQUE
				If duplicate request comes:
					DuplicateKeyException
				Example:
					CREATE TABLE payments(
					 id BIGINT,
					 transaction_id VARCHAR UNIQUE
					)
			=> If same transaction sent again ΓÁÈ DB rejects it.

		3. Optimistic Locking
				Useful when updating the same record.
				Example:
					balance
					version
				If two updates occur simultaneously ΓÁÈ one fails.
					Used with:
					@Version -> in JPA.

		4. Distributed Lock (Redis)
					Useful in microservices.
				Example:
					SETNX payment_lock
					If lock exists ΓÁÈ reject request.
				Flow:
					Request arrives
					Acquire Redis lock
					Process payment
					Release lock

		5. UI Level Prevention
				Example:
					Disable submit button
				Angular / React:
					button.disabled = true
					This prevents double click

286. What happens when we run a Java program ?
		=> When we run a Java program, the JVM starts and the ClassLoader loads the .class file. The class goes through loading, 
		   linking, and initialization phases. After that, the JVM looks for the public static void main(String[] args) method. 
		   A main thread is created and execution starts from the main method

287. Difference between Thread vs Runnable.
		=> Both are used to create threads, but they differ in design and flexibility.

		1∩╕ÂΓâú Thread : Thread is a class in Java.
				=> You create a thread by extending the Thread class.
					Example:
						class MyThread extends Thread {
						    public void run() {
						        System.out.println("Thread is running");
						    }
						}
						
						public class Test {
						    public static void main(String[] args) {
						        MyThread t = new MyThread();
						        t.start();
						    }
						}

		2∩╕ÂΓâú Runnable : Runnable is a functional interface.
				You implement it and pass it to a Thread.
			Example
				class MyRunnable implements Runnable {
				    public void run() {
				        System.out.println("Thread is running");
				    }
				}
				
				public class Test {
				    public static void main(String[] args) {
				        Thread t = new Thread(new MyRunnable());
				        t.start();
				    }
				}

	=> Thread is a class used to create threads by extending it and overriding the run() method. 
	   Runnable is an interface that represents a task to be executed by a thread. 
	   Runnable is preferred because it allows multiple inheritance and better resource sharing between threads.

288. Common Jenkins Pipeline Stages ?
		1. Checkout / Source :
			Pull code from Git (GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket)
		2. Build :
			Compile the code
			Example: mvn clean install (for Java/Spring Boot)
		3. Static Code Analysis (SonarQube) :
			Before testing, the code quality is analyzed using SonarQube.
				Checks performed:
					Code smells
					Bugs
					Vulnerabilities
					Code coverage
					Technical debt
					Security issues
		4.Test :
			Run unit tests, integration tests
		5. Package / Artifact
			Create build artifact
			Example: .jar, .war, Docker image
			
		6. Publish Artifact
			Upload to artifact repository
			Example: Nexus, Artifactory
			
		7. Deploy (Last Stage)
			Deploy application to environment
			Example:
			Dev
			QA
			Staging
			Production

289. How do you configure SonarQube in a project ?
		1∩╕ÂΓâú What is SonarQube
			SonarQube is a static code analysis tool used to detect:
				Bugs
				Code smells
				Security vulnerabilities
				Code coverage
				Duplicate code
			It helps maintain code quality and enforce coding standards.

		2∩╕ÂΓâú Basic Steps to Configure SonarQube :

			Step 1 ΓÇõ Install SonarQube Server
				Usually hosted on:
					Local server
					Docker
					Cloud server
				Example Docker:
					docker run -d --name sonarqube -p 9000:9000 sonarqube
				Access UI
					http://localhost:9000

			Step 2 ΓÇõ Create Project in SonarQube
					Inside SonarQube UI:
						Projects ΓÁÈ Create Project
					Generate:
						Project Key
						Authentication Token
					Example:
						projectKey=my-app
						token=abc123
			Step 3 ΓÇõ Add Sonar Scanner to Project
					For Maven Spring Boot project
					Add plugin in pom.xml
						<plugin>
						 <groupId>org.sonarsource.scanner.maven</groupId>
						 <artifactId>sonar-maven-plugin</artifactId>
						 <version>3.9.1.2184</version>
						</plugin>

			Step 4 ΓÇõ Configure Sonar Properties
					Create sonar-project.properties
						sonar.projectKey=my-app
						sonar.projectName=MyApp
						sonar.projectVersion=1.0
						
						sonar.sources=src/main/java
						sonar.tests=src/test/java
						
						sonar.java.binaries=target/classes
						sonar.host.url=http://localhost:9000
						sonar.login=token

290. Runnable vs Thread ΓÇõ When should we use each ?
		In Java, there are two ways to create a thread:
			1∩╕ÂΓâú Extend java.lang.Thread
			2∩╕ÂΓâú Implement java.lang.Runnable

	1∩╕ÂΓâú Using Runnable Interface (Recommended)
		 Example :
			class MyTask implements Runnable {
			    @Override
			    public void run() {
			        System.out.println("Task running by " + Thread.currentThread().getName());
			    }
			}
			
			public class Main {
			    public static void main(String[] args) {
			        MyTask task = new MyTask();
			        Thread t = new Thread(task);
			        t.start();
			    }
			}

			When should we use Runnable?
				Use Runnable when your class needs to extend another class.
			Example:
				class EmployeeService extends BaseService implements Runnable
				Java does not support multiple inheritance, so if you extend Thread, you cannot extend any other class.
			Advantages
				Γ£õ Better design (separation of task and thread)
				Γ£õ Allows class to extend other classes
				Γ£õ Used with Executor Framework
				Γ£õ Used in thread pools
			
			Example with executor:
				ExecutorService executor = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(5);
				executor.submit(new MyTask());
		=> For modern Java applications, especially multithreaded environments (which youΓÇÕre interested in), 
		   Runnable is preferred.

	2∩╕ÂΓâú Using Thread Class
			Example
			class MyThread extends Thread {
			    @Override
			    public void run() {
			        System.out.println("Thread running");
			    }
			}
			
			public class Main {
			    public static void main(String[] args) {
			        MyThread t = new MyThread();
			        t.start();
			    }
			}
			When should we use Thread?
			
			Use Thread class when:
				Γ£õ You want to customize thread behavior
				Γ£õ You need to override thread methods
			
			Example:
			class MyThread extends Thread {
			
			    public MyThread() {
			        setName("Worker-Thread");
			    }
			
			    @Override
			    public void run() {
			        System.out.println(getName());
			    }
			}
		=> But this approach is less flexible.

	=> | Feature      | Runnable                 | Thread                      |
	   | ------------ | ------------------------ | --------------------------- |
	   | Type         | Interface                | Class                       |
	   | Inheritance  | Can extend other classes | Cannot extend another class |
	   | Design       | Better separation        | Task tightly coupled        |
	   | Thread Pool  | Supported                | Not recommended             |
	   | Modern usage | Preferred                | Rare                        |

291. How can we implement multithreading in Java ?
	=> Real Project Usage (Important for Interview)
			In Spring Boot applications, we usually use:
				ExecutorService
				CompletableFuture
				@Async
			Example:
				@Async
				public void processOrder() {
				    // background processing
				}

292. Causes of dead lock accurs ? and prevntive methods ?
	=> Deadlock occurs when these 4 conditions exist simultaneously
		1∩╕ÂΓâú Mutual Exclusion ΓÇô Resource can be used by only one thread at a time
		2∩╕ÂΓâú Hold and Wait ΓÇô Thread holds one resource and waits for another
		3∩╕ÂΓâú No Preemption ΓÇô Resource cannot be forcibly taken away
		4∩╕ÂΓâú Circular Wait ΓÇô Threads wait in a circular dependency
	=> If we break any one of these, deadlock can be prevented.

	=> Ways to Prevent Deadlock in Java
		1∩╕ÂΓâú Lock Ordering (Most Common Solution)
			Always acquire locks in the same order.
			Problem Example
				synchronized(resource1){
				    synchronized(resource2){
				        // work
				    }
				}
			
			Another thread:
				synchronized(resource2){
				    synchronized(resource1){
				        // deadlock
				    }
				}

		2∩╕ÂΓâú Using tryLock()
			Using java.util.concurrent.locks.ReentrantLock with timeout prevents threads from waiting forever.
			 Example:
				Lock lock1 = new ReentrantLock();
				Lock lock2 = new ReentrantLock();
				if(lock1.tryLock()){
				    try{
				        if(lock2.tryLock()){
				            try{
				                // critical section
				            } finally {
				                lock2.unlock();
				            }
				        }
				    } finally {
				        lock1.unlock();
				    }
				}
			=> If the lock is unavailable, the thread doesn't wait indefinitely.

		3∩╕ÂΓâú Avoid Nested Locks
			 Avoid acquiring multiple locks inside each other when possible.
				Bad design:
					Lock A
					   ΓÁÈ Lock B
					Better design:
			=> Single lock for shared resource

		4∩╕ÂΓâú Use Timeout While Waiting
			Instead of waiting forever:
				tryLock(5, TimeUnit.SECONDS)
				If the lock isn't acquired within time ΓÁÈ thread exits safely.

		5∩╕ÂΓâú Use Higher-Level Concurrency Utilities
				Classes from java.util.concurrent help reduce deadlocks:
			Examples:
				ExecutorService
				ConcurrentHashMap
				BlockingQueue
				These handle synchronization internally.
			Real Project Practice
				In real enterprise applications (Spring Boot / microservices):
			We avoid deadlocks by:
				Using ExecutorService thread pools
				Avoiding nested synchronization
				Using Concurrent collections
				Using database transaction isolation properly

293. What is Mutext ? -> Mutex stands for Mutual Exclusion
	=> It is a synchronization mechanism used in multithreading to ensure that only one thread can access a shared 			   resource at a time

	=> How Mutex Works :
		A thread acquires the lock
		It enters the critical section
		Other threads must wait
		When the thread finishes, it releases the lock

294. what is Semaphore ? 
	=> A Semaphore is a synchronization mechanism used in multithreading to control how many threads can access a shared 	   resource at the same time. ≡ÓÜª
	=> Unlike Mutex, which allows only one thread, a Semaphore can allow multiple threads.
	=> A Semaphore is a counter-based lock that restricts the number of threads accessing a resource concurrently.
	=> Example
			Suppose we have a database connection pool of size 3.
				Semaphore value = 3
				Only 3 threads can access the database at the same time
				Other threads must wait

	=> | Feature   | Mutex                       | Semaphore                |
	   | --------- | --------------------------- | ------------------------ |
	   | Access    | Only **1 thread**           | **Multiple threads**     |
	   | Lock type | Exclusive lock              | Counter based            |
	   | Ownership | Same thread must unlock     | Any thread can release   |
	   | Use case  | Critical section protection | Resource pool management |

295. What is @PostConstruct and when to use it ?
		=> @PostConstruct runs automatically after Spring creates the object and injects all dependencies.

		=> Lifecycle Flow in Spring Bean
				When Spring creates a bean, the lifecycle is:
					=> Bean Instantiation (object created)
					=> Dependency Injection
					=> @PostConstruct method executes
					=> Bean is ready for use

		=> When Do We Use @PostConstruct ?
			1∩╕ÂΓâú Initialize data after dependency injection
				 -> Sometimes a method needs injected dependencies.

				Eg :	@Service
						public class CacheService {
						    @Autowired
						    RedisTemplate redisTemplate;
						
						    @PostConstruct
						    public void loadCache() {
						        System.out.println("Loading cache from Redis");
						    }
						}
			2∩╕ÂΓâú Preload data when application starts
					Example:
						Load configurations
						Load reference data
						Warm up cache

			3∩╕ÂΓâú Setup connections or resources
					Example:
						initialize Kafka consumer
						initialize cache
						initialize thread pool

		Note : Rules of @PostConstruct :
					Γ£õ Method must be void
					Γ£õ Method should not have parameters
					Γ£õ Runs only once per bean

		=> @PreDestroy :
			-> Runs when the bean is about to be destroyed.
					@PreDestroy
					public void cleanup(){
					    System.out.println("Bean is destroyed");
					}

296. What is the difference between clustered index vs non-clustered index ?

		| Feature        | Clustered Index        | Non-Clustered Index   |
		| -------------- | ---------------------- | --------------------- |
		| Data storage   | Data stored with index | Separate structure    |
		| Physical order | Changes table order    | Does not change order |
		| Number allowed | Only **1**             | Multiple              |
		| Lookup speed   | Faster                 | Slightly slower       |
		| Example use    | Primary key            | Search columns        |

297. What is Load Testing ?
	=> Load testing is used to verify how an application performs under expected user load and to identify performance 		   bottlenecks such as slow APIs, memory issues, or database contention.

	=> Tools Used for Load Testing :
		Common tools used:
			1. Apache JMeter
			2. Gatling
			3. k6
			4. LoadRunner
		=> In most projects we commonly use JMeter or k6. 

	=> Steps I Follow to Perform Load Testing :
		 1∩╕ÂΓâú Identify Critical APIs / Flows
					First identify the high traffic APIs.
				Example:
					Login API
					Search API
					Payment API
					Dashboard API
			=> These APIs are tested first because they receive the most traffic.

		2∩╕ÂΓâú Create Test Scripts :
					Using JMeter / k6, create scripts to simulate user actions.
				Example in JMeter:
					Thread Group ΓÁÈ Simulates users
					HTTP Request ΓÁÈ API call
					Assertions ΓÁÈ Validate response
					Listeners ΓÁÈ Collect results

		3∩╕ÂΓâú Run Tests with Gradual Load
					We do ramp-up testing.
				Example:
					Users	Ramp Time
					100	1 min
					500	5 min
					1000	10 min
				This helps understand when performance degrades.

		 4∩╕ÂΓâú Monitor System Metrics
			-> During the test we monitor:
				Application Metrics:
						Response time
						Throughput
						Error rate
				Infrastructure Metrics:
					CPU usage
					Memory usage
					Thread count
					DB connections
				Monitoring tools used:
					Dynatrace
					Prometheus
					Grafana

		5∩╕ÂΓâú Identify Bottlenecks
				Common bottlenecks:
					Slow database queries
					Connection pool exhaustion
					Thread pool limits
					Memory leaks
					External API latency

		6∩╕ÂΓâú Optimize the System
				After finding issues we improve:
					Example improvements:
						Add DB indexes
						Enable caching (Redis)
						Increase thread pools
						Optimize SQL queries
						Implement API rate limiting

		=> We perform load testing using tools like JMeter or k6 by simulating concurrent users hitting critical APIs. 
		   We gradually increase load, monitor system metrics such as response time, throughput, CPU, and memory using  		   tools like Dynatrace and Grafana, identify bottlenecks such as slow DB queries or thread pool limits, optimize 		   the system, and re-run tests to validate improvements

298. Immutable class and Singleton class example
	1. Immutable class :
			final class Person {
			    private final String name;
			    private final int age;
			
			    public Person(String name, int age) {
			        this.name = name;
			        this.age = age;
			    }
			
			    public String getName() {
			        return name;
			    }
			
			    public int getAge() {
			        return age;
			    }
			}

	2. Singleton class :
		public class Singleton {
		    private static Singleton instance;
		    private Singleton() {}
		    public static synchronized Singleton getInstance() {
		        if(instance == null){
		            instance = new Singleton();
		        }
		        return instance;
		    }
		}

299. What are GitHub Actions ?
	=> GitHub Actions is a CI/CD (Continuous Integration / Continuous Deployment) tool built inside GitHub.
	=> It allows you to automatically build, test, and deploy your code whenever something happens in the repository.

	Example: 
		=> Developer pushes code ΓÁÈ GitHub Actions runs build ΓÁÈ runs tests ΓÁÈ deploys application.

		Workflow :
			A workflow is the automation process defined in a YAML file.
	Steps :
		Each job contains steps.
		Example:
			checkout code
			install dependencies
			build project
			run tests

300. What is a Thread Dump ?
	=> A thread dump is a snapshot of all running threads in the JVM at a specific moment.
			It helps you identify:
				Deadlocks
				Threads stuck in waiting state
				High CPU threads
				Blocked threads

	=> What a Thread Dump File Looks Like : Thread dump is a text file.
			"http-nio-8080-exec-10" #45 daemon prio=5 os_prio=0 tid=0x00007f8c8400 nid=0x2a waiting on condition
			   java.lang.Thread.State: WAITING (parking)
			        at java.util.concurrent.locks.LockSupport.park()
			        at java.util.concurrent.locks.AbstractQueuedSynchronizer.acquire()
			
			"ForkJoinPool.commonPool-worker-1" #23 daemon prio=5 tid=0x00007f8c8500 nid=0x3b runnable
			   java.lang.Thread.State: RUNNABLE
			        at java.util.HashMap.get()

		Key things inside:
			Thread name
			Thread ID
			Thread state
			Stack trace

	=>	| State         | Meaning              |
		| ------------- | -------------------- |
		| RUNNABLE      | Thread executing     |
		| BLOCKED       | Waiting for lock     |
		| WAITING       | Waiting indefinitely |
		| TIMED_WAITING | Waiting with timeout |
		| TERMINATED    | Thread finished      |

	=> How to Generate Thread Dump ?
			Method 1 ΓÇõ Using jstack
				Find process ID:
					jps
				Example:
					12345 MySpringBootApp
				Generate thread dump:
					jstack 12345 > threaddump.txt

==> What is Heap Dump?
		A heap dump is a snapshot of memory used by the JVM.
			It contains:
				All objects in memory
				Memory allocation
				Object references
			Used to detect:
				Memory leaks
				OutOfMemoryError
				Large objects

Note : They are stored in the server filesystem (disk), not in system memory.


301. What is Serialization ?
	=> Serialization = converting a Java object into a byte stream so that it can be: stored, transferred over 									network, cached
	=>	Deserialization = converting that byte stream back into an object.

	Real-Time Example: Session Storage (Very Common)
		=>	Suppose a user logs into a banking system.
				User Login
				   ΓÁô
				Spring Boot Server
				   ΓÁô
				User Session Created
			
			The session contains:
				class UserSession implements Serializable {
				    String userId;
				    String role;
				    String token;
				}
			=>	This object is serialized before storing.

		=> Where Serialized Data is Stored :
				Serialized objects can be stored in:
					1∩╕ÂΓâú File system -> session.ser
					2∩╕ÂΓâú Database -> Stored as BLOB
					3∩╕ÂΓâú Distributed cache -> Redis

	Eg :    import java.io.Serializable;
			class Employee implements Serializable {
			    int id;
			    String name;
			
			    Employee(int id, String name){
			        this.id = id;
			        this.name = name;
			    }
			}

			Serialize Object :
				FileOutputStream file = new FileOutputStream("employee.ser");
				ObjectOutputStream out = new ObjectOutputStream(file);
				
					Employee emp = new Employee(101, "Manju");
					
					out.writeObject(emp);
					out.close();
					file.close();
				
			=> 	Now object stored in file: employee.ser
