303. what is @Transctional propagation :
		=> @Transactional propagation defines how a transaction behaves when one transactional method calls another 			   transactional method

		=> Propagation decides whether a method should join an existing transaction or start a new one.

		eg:	OrderService.placeOrder()
			       |
			       |---- PaymentService.makePayment()
			       |
			       |---- InventoryService.updateStock()

			Now question is:
				≡ÓÀÊ Should all these methods run in one transaction
					(or)
				≡ÓÀÊ Should some run in separate transactions
			=> This behavior is controlled using Propagation.
	
		=> Most Important Propagations
				REQUIRED
				REQUIRES_NEW
				SUPPORTS

304. How version are maintained in springboot application ?
	1∩╕ÂΓâú What is a SNAPSHOT Version ?
		In Maven/Spring Boot projects, versions are usually defined in pom.xml.
	Example:
		<version>1.0.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
	Meaning :
			Version				Meaning
			1.0.0				Stable release version
			1.0.0-SNAPSHOT		Development version (still changing)

	A SNAPSHOT version means:
		=> The build is not final
		=> Code can change anytime
		=> Maven may download updated builds automatically
	==> So developers use SNAPSHOT during development and release versions for production.

	eg:	1.0.0-SNAPSHOT   ΓÁÈ development
		1.0.0            ΓÁÈ first stable release
		1.0.1-SNAPSHOT   ΓÁÈ development for next patch
		1.0.1            ΓÁÈ bug fix release
		1.1.0-SNAPSHOT   ΓÁÈ development for new features
		1.1.0            ΓÁÈ minor release

305. What is @emabaded and @Embadable ?
	=> In JPA / Hibernate, @Embeddable is used to define a class whose fields can be embedded inside another entity 		   instead of creating a separate table.
	=> @Embeddable marks a class as reusable component whose fields become part of the parent entity table.

	Eg: Suppose a user has an address.
		Instead of creating another table, we embed it.

	1. Embeddable Class
		import jakarta.persistence.Embeddable;
			@Embeddable
			public class Address {
			
			    private String city;
			    private String state;
			    private String zipCode;
			}
	2. Entity Class :
		@Entity
		public class User {
		
		    @Id
		    private Long id;
		
		    private String name;
		
		    @Embedded
		    private Address address;
		}

=>	| Annotation    | Purpose                                |
	| ------------- | -------------------------------------- |
	| `@Embeddable` | Defines reusable value object          |
	| `@Embedded`   | Used inside entity to embed the object |

306. What are the deployment strategies ?
	=> Deployment strategies define how a new version of an application is released to production without affecting users.

	1∩╕ÂΓâú Recreate Deployment
			Old version is stopped first, then new version starts.
			Old Version (V1) ΓÁÈ STOP
			                    ΓÁô
			                Start V2
			Pros :
				Very simple
			Cons :
				Downtime occurs
			Example:
				Users cannot access application for few seconds/minutes

	2∩╕ÂΓâú Rolling Deployment
			=> New instances are gradually replaced with new versions.
					V1 V1 V1 V1
					ΓÁô
					V2 V1 V1 V1
					ΓÁô
					V2 V2 V1 V1
					ΓÁô
					V2 V2 V2 V2
			Pros :
				No downtime
				Gradual update
			Cons :
				Both versions run simultaneously

	3∩╕ÂΓâú Blue-Green Deployment
			Two environments exist:
				Blue ΓÁÈ Current Production
				Green ΓÁÈ New Version
			Flow:
				Users ΓÁÈ Blue
				Deploy V2 ΓÁÈ Green
				Switch traffic ΓÁÈ Green
			Pros
				Instant rollback
				No downtime
			Cons
				Requires double infrastructure
			Example:
				Blue = v1
				Green = v2
			If problem occurs:
				Traffic ΓÁÈ Blue again

	4∩╕ÂΓâú Canary Deployment
			Release new version to small percentage of users first.
				90% ΓÁÈ Old version
				10% ΓÁÈ New version
			If everything works:
				50% ΓÁÈ New version
				100% ΓÁÈ New version
			Pros :
				Safer deployment
				Detect issues early
				Used by large companies like Netflix.

	5∩╕ÂΓâú A/B Testing Deployment
		=>	Different versions are released to different groups of users.
			Example:
				Group A ΓÁÈ Version 1
				Group B ΓÁÈ Version 2
			Used to test:
				UI changes
				new features
				performance

307. Default Fetch Strategies ?

		| Mapping Type  | Default Fetch Type |
		| ------------- | ------------------ |
		| `@ManyToOne`  | **EAGER**          |
		| `@OneToOne`   | **EAGER**          |
		| `@OneToMany`  | **LAZY**           |
		| `@ManyToMany` | **LAZY**           |

308. How do you secure method-level in Spring Boot ?
		=> This allows you to control who can call specific methods based on roles, permissions, or conditions.

	Γ£à Step 1: Enable Method-Level Security
			In your configuration class:
				@Configuration
				@EnableMethodSecurity   // Spring Boot 3+
				public class SecurityConfig {
				}

	Γ£à Step 2: Use Method-Level Annotations
			≡Óõ╣ 1. @PreAuthorize (Most Common)
				=> Checks before method execution :
						@PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')")
						public void deleteUser(Long id) {
						    // only ADMIN can call
						}
				≡ÓÀÊ With multiple roles:
						@PreAuthorize("hasAnyRole('ADMIN','MANAGER')")
				≡ÓÀÊ Using method parameters:
						@PreAuthorize("#id == authentication.principal.id")
						public User getUser(Long id) {
						    return userRepository.findById(id);
						}
			≡Óõ╣ 2. @PostAuthorize
				=> Checks after method execution :
					@PostAuthorize("returnObject.owner == authentication.name")
					public Document getDocument(Long id) {
					    return docRepository.findById(id);
					}

			≡Óõ╣ 3. @Secured
					=> Simple role-based check
							@Secured("ROLE_ADMIN")
							public void updateUser() {
							}

309. Hibernate Entity Lifecycle ?
		=> An entity in Hibernate goes through 4 main states:
			1∩╕ÂΓâú Transient State :
				≡ÓÀÊ Object is just created using new
				≡ÓÀÊ Not associated with Hibernate session
				≡ÓÀÊ Not stored in DB
				
				Employee emp = new Employee();  // transient
				emp.setName("John");
				
				Γ£õ No DB interaction
				Γ£õ No primary key (usually)

			2∩╕ÂΓâú Persistent State :
				≡ÓÀÊ Object is associated with Session (Persistence Context)
				≡ÓÀÊ Changes are automatically tracked (Dirty Checking)
				
				Session session = sessionFactory.openSession();
				session.beginTransaction();
				
				Employee emp = new Employee();
				emp.setName("John");
				
				session.save(emp);  // now persistent
				
				Γ£õ Stored in DB (or will be on flush/commit)
				Γ£õ Hibernate tracks changes automatically

			3∩╕ÂΓâú Detached State :
				≡ÓÀÊ Session is closed or object is evicted
				≡ÓÀÊ Entity is no longer tracked by Hibernate
					
				session.close();  // emp becomes detached
					Γ£õ Exists in DB
					ΓÙÔ Changes NOT tracked automatically
				To reattach:
					session.update(emp);

			4∩╕ÂΓâú Removed (Deleted) State :
				≡ÓÀÊ Entity marked for deletion
					session.delete(emp);
					Γ£õ Will be removed from DB on commit

			=> ≡Óõã Lifecycle Flow
				Transient ΓÁÈ Persistent ΓÁÈ Detached ΓÁÈ Removed

310. update() vs merge() in Hibernate ?
		≡Óõ╣ update()
			Γ£à What it does
				Reattaches a detached entity to the session
				Same object becomes persistent
				session.update(emp);
			≡ÓõÑ Behavior
				No copy created
				Same object is reused
				Faster (no extra work)

		≡Óõ╣ merge()
			Γ£à What it does
				Copies state of detached object ΓÁÈ into a new managed entity
				Returns a new persistent object
				Employee managedEmp = session.merge(emp);

311. Time complexity for all the collections :
		| Collection    | Get/Search | Insert   | Delete   |
		| ------------- | ---------- | -------- | -------- |
		| ArrayList     | O(1)       | O(1)*    | O(n)     |
		| LinkedList    | O(n)       | O(1)     | O(n)     |
		| HashMap       | O(1)       | O(1)     | O(1)     |
		| TreeMap       | O(log n)   | O(log n) | O(log n) |
		| HashSet       | O(1)       | O(1)     | O(1)     |
		| TreeSet       | O(log n)   | O(log n) | O(log n) |
		| PriorityQueue | O(1) peek  | O(log n) | O(log n) |

	≡ÓÀÊ DTO = Data transfer representation

		| ---------------- | ---------------- |
		| HandlerMapping   | Finds controller |
		| HandlerAdapter   | Executes method  |

1. Create a custom validators to check pass strength
	Eg : this.userGroup = this.fb.group({
			username  : ['', Validators.required, Validators.pattern("")],
			password : ['', [this.strongPasswordValidator()]]
		})
		
		 strongPasswordValidator(){
			return (control: AbstractControl)=> {
			  const value = control.value;
			  if(!value){
				return null;
			  }

			  const strong = 
			  /[A_Z]/.test(value) &&
			  /[a-z]/.test(value) &&
			  /[0-9]/.test(value) &&
			  value.length >= 8;

			  return strong;

			};
		}

			transform(value: any) {

			}
		}

30. DDL v/s DML real time use case	

	=> DDL (Data Definition Language) is used to define or modify database structure (schema).
	
	| Command  | Purpose                             |
	| -------- | ----------------------------------- |
	| CREATE   | Create table/database               |
	| ALTER    | Modify table structure              |
	| DROP     | Delete table                        |
	| TRUNCATE | Remove all rows (structure remains) |
	
	DML (Data Manipulation Language) is used to manipulate actual table data.
	
	| Command | Purpose     |
	| ------- | ----------- |
	| INSERT  | Add data    |
	| UPDATE  | Modify data |
	| DELETE  | Remove data |
	| SELECT  | Fetch data  |


	
	
31. Views, procedures, triigers

	≡ÓÀÊ What is a View?
	=> These are used to fetch the data from table, a vtirual table can be created using sql queries.
	=> not used to store only fetch
	
	≡ÓÀÊ What is Stored Procedure?
	=> A Stored Procedure is a precompiled block of SQL logic stored in database.
	
	≡ÓÀÊ What is Trigger?
	=> A Trigger is SQL block of code that automatically excute when an event accurs
		Events:
			INSERT
			UPDATE 
			DELETE
			

32. Where does the Kafka stores the data ?

	=> kafka stores the data on the disk(file system) of the Kafka Broker servers.
	
	Internally 
	-> Each Topic -> split into Partition
	-> Each Partion -> stored as log files on disk
	
	=> Kafka is disk-based (not memory based like Redis)
	
	
33. How does Kafka maintain version ?

	=> Kafka does not use the work version -> it uses Offset
	=> Each message has a unique sequentail offset number
	Eg:
		Partition-0
		--------------
		Offset 0 ΓÁÈ Order Created
		Offset 1 ΓÁÈ Payment Done
		Offset 2 ΓÁÈ Order Shipped
		
		=> Kafka knows which message alreay consumed and what is next
		
34. How long does kafka keep data ?
	
	=> Kafka keeps the data based on Retention policy:
		2 types 
			1. Time based retention -> can configured -> eg: log.retention.hours = 168  ->  once 168 hours done -> Old segments are deleted automatically
			2. size based retention -> can configured -> eg: log.retention.bytes = 10GB ->  If topic exceeds 10GB ΓÁÈ old data deleted
			
	
35. Kafka Architecture :

	Producer
		ΓÁô
	Kafka Broker (Disk Storage)
		ΓÁô
	Consumer

36. how does kafka handle backup/safety ?
	=> Replication factor
		-> replication.factor = 3
		
		| Question                | Answer                       |
		| ----------------------- | ---------------------------- |
		| Where stored?           | Broker disk (log segments)   |
		| How version maintained? | Using OFFSET                 |
		| How long stored?        | Retention policy (time/size) |
		| Physical location?      | Broker server file system    |
		| Backup?                 | Replication factor           |
		
	=> when you'll get memory execption in kafka ?
			1. Broker-Side Memory Issues (Most Critical)
			
				ΓÙÔ Huge Message Size -> Producer sends messages larger than broker limits
				ΓÙÔ Too Many Partitions -> ~2,000ΓÇô4,000 partitions per broker (depends on RAM)
				ΓÙÔ High Fetch/Produce Throughput -> Large batches + slow disk/network
				
			2. Consumer-Side Memory Exceptions
				-> Too many records loaded into memory at once
			3. Log Retention & Disk Backpressure
		
37. which design pattern you worked on ?
	≡Óõ╣ 1) Singleton Design Pattern (Most Common)
		=> In Spring, Beans are Singleton by default.
		
				Example:  Spring creates only one object of this class and reuses it.
				
					=> Service classes
					=> Repository classes
					=> Configuration classes
					=> Utility classes

	≡Óõ╣ 2) Factory Design Pattern (Very Important)
		=> Used when object creation logic should be hidden.
		=> We used Factory pattern to create different service implementations dynamically.
		
				Example:
					In your project:
						≡ÓÀÊ Payment Service
						≡ÓÀÊ Notification Service
						≡ÓÀÊ Report Generator
						
	≡Óõ╣ 3) Builder Design Pattern
			
		=> Used when object has many fields.
		
				Example:
					DTO / Request Object creation
					User user = User.builder()
						.name("Roy")
						.age(25)
						.city("Bangalore")
						.build();
						
	≡Óõ╣ 5) Observer Pattern
		=> Used in:
			Kafka consumers
			Event listeners
			Spring Application Events
			
			Example:
				Producer publishes event
				Multiple consumers listen to it.

38. what is volatile key word ? can valatile ensure thread safety ?

	==> The valatile keyword ensure visbility of changes to varible across threads.
	==> Note :  No guarrantee thread safety or atomicity
		
		
39. Γ£à What is AWS Lambda ?

	==> AWS lambda is serverless compute service by AWS, that let's you run code without managing servers
	
	==> You only:
	
			=> Upload your code
			=> Configure a trigger
			=> AWS automatically handles scaling, provisioning, patching, and infrastructure
			
	==> ≡Óõù How AWS Lambda Integrates With Other AWS Services
	
			==> AWS Lambda is event-driven, meaning it is triggered by other AWS services.
				 
				Eg : Client ΓÁÈ API Gateway ΓÁÈ Lambda ΓÁÈ Response
					 File Upload ΓÁÈ S3 Event ΓÁÈ Lambda
				 
40. Γ£à What are Runnable and Callable Interfaces in Java?

	==> ≡ÓÀÊ YES ΓÇõ Both Runnable and Callable are Functional Interfaces Γ£à
	
	==> Runnable : void run();
	
			≡ÓôÔ Key Points
				Γ£õ Does NOT return result
				Γ£õ Cannot throw checked exception
				Γ£õ Used with Thread class or ExecutorService
				Γ£õ Old and simple interface
				
			Eg : class MyTask implements Runnable {
					public void run() {
						System.out.println("Task running...");
					}
				}

				public class Main {
					public static void main(String[] args) {
						Thread t = new Thread(new MyTask());
						t.start();
					}
					}
	==> Callable Interface : V call() throws Exception;
	
			≡ÓôÔ Key Points
				Γ£õ Returns a result
				Γ£õ Can throw checked exception
				Γ£õ Used with ExecutorService
				Γ£õ Introduced in Java 5
				
				
41. Γ£à What is Intrinsic Lock in Java?

	==> An intrinis lock is the internal moniter lock that every java object has, 
		which automatically aquired and released when a tread enters and exit syncronized block
		
		EG : ≡Óºá Key Points
				Γ£õ Every Java object has one intrinsic lock
				Γ£õ Managed automatically by JVM
				Γ£õ Used by synchronized
				Γ£õ Only one thread can hold it at a time
				Γ£õ Ensures mutual exclusion + visibility
				
	==> class Counter {
	
			public synchronized void increment() {
					System.out.println("Thread safe operation");
				}
			}
			
			When thread enters increment():
			≡ÓÀÊ Acquires intrinsic lock of Counter object (this)
			≡ÓÀÊ Executes method
			≡ÓÀÊ Releases lock after completion

42. Γ£à What is Race Condition?
	==> A race condtion happens when multiple threads compete to update shared data without proper synchronization,
		causing unpredicatble output
		
	==> to avoid this we can synchronized keyword 
		Eg :
		public void increment() {
			synchronized(this) {
				count++;
			}
		}
		
43. End-to-end flow of how an Entity class eventually becomes a table in the database (JPA ΓÁÈ Hibernate ΓÁÈ SQL)

	==> When Spring Boot starts, it scans entity classes and passes metadata to Hibernate through JPA. 
		Hibernate generates SQL based on entity mappings and ddl-auto configuration, 
		and executes it via JDBC to create database tables.

	
44. ≡Óºá Internal Working for @Repository

	==> It:
		1∩╕Â. Creates proxy around class
		2∩╕Â. Adds exception translation interceptor
		3∩╕Â. Catches DB exceptions
		4∩╕Â. Converts to Spring standard exceptions

		@Service

		}

		| --------------------- | ------------------------------ |

		| Exception Translation | Γ£à Yes (because of @Repository) |
		| Recommended           | ΓÙÔ No                           |

			To provide:
			Γ£õ Thread safety
			Γ£õ High concurrency
			Γ£õ Better performance
			Γ£õ Lock-free reads
			Γ£õ Fine-grained locking

					HttpStatus.INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR

		}
	}

	  console.log(err);
	})

6. const arr = [1, [2, [3, 4]], 5];

	function flattenArray(array){
	  let result = []
	  array.forEach(element => {
		if(Array.isArray(element)){
		   result = result.concat(flattenArray(element));
		}else{
		  result.push(element)
		}
	  });
	   return result;
	}
	console.log(flattenArray(arr)); //[1,2,3,4,5]

==============================================  Stream API questions : ==================================================================

1. String str = "this is a test. This test is only a test." Output: [test=3, is=3, this=2, a=2, only=1] using java 8 stream api

	=> solution : String str = "this is a test. This test is only a test.";
			      Map<String, Long> collect = Arrays.stream(str.split(" ")).collect(groupingBy(Function.identity(), counting()));

	=> to ignore special char (.) and case sensitivity

	String str = "this is a test. This test is only a test.";

        Map<String, Long> collect = Arrays.stream(str.split(" "))
                .map(l-> l.toLowerCase())
                .map(l-> l.replaceAll("[^a-zA-Z]",""))
                .collect(Collectors.groupingBy(Function.identity(),Collectors.counting()));

        System.out.println(collect);
	

2. String input = "swiss";

	==> solution :
			String input = "swiss";
			String s = Arrays.stream(input.split("")).collect(groupingBy(Function.identity(), counting())).entrySet().stream().filter(n -> n.getValue() == 1).map(Map.Entry::getKey).findFirst().orElse("");
			System.out.println(s);

 
3. Collectors.groupingBy() and Collectors.partitioningBy()?

4. String input="a-1,b-2,c-3,a-4,b-5,c-6,a-7";
 
	o/p	a[1, 4, 7]
		b[2, 5]
		c[3, 6]
		
	=> solution : Map<String, List<Integer>> collect = Arrays.stream(input.split(","))
                .map(n -> n.split("-"))
                .collect(groupingBy(key -> key[0], mapping(key -> Integer.parseInt(key[1])
                        , toList())));

        System.out.println(collect);

9. Java Program to figure out sum of second lowest and second highest number from an Array

	Solution :	List<Integer> numbers = List.of(5, 1, 9, 2, 8, 3);
        Integer collect = numbers.stream().distinct().sorted().collect(collectingAndThen(toList(), a -> a.get(1) + a.get(a.size() - 2)));

                .collect(Collectors.toList());

22. Filter palindrome words from a list using streams

      List<String> words = Arrays.asList("madam", "racecar", "hello", "level", "world", "radar");
        List<String> collect = words.stream().filter(word -> isPalindromeWord(word)).collect(toList());
        System.out.println(collect);
		}

		public static  boolean isPalindromeWord(String word){
			String reversed = new StringBuffer(word).reverse().toString();
			return word.equals(reversed);
		}

35. Sort by Multiple Fields :

	1. Ascending :
		List<Employee> sorted = employees.stream()
	    .sorted(Comparator.comparing(Employee::getAge)
	            .thenComparing(Employee::getDepartment)
	            .thenComparing(Employee::getSalary))
	    .collect(Collectors.toList());

	2. Descending:
		List<Employee> sorted = employees.stream()
	    .sorted(Comparator.comparing(Employee::getAge)
	            .thenComparing(Employee::getDepartment)
	            .thenComparing(Employee::getSalary)
	            .reversed())
	    .collect(Collectors.toList());

=>  What if thenComparing(Employee::getDepartment) returns null?
	What happens?
	How to handle it?

	≡ÓÀÊ NullPointerException will occur
	Because internally:
		e1.getDepartment().compareTo(e2.getDepartment())
		And calling compareTo() on null throws NPE.

=> ≡Óõ╖ How To Handle Null Safely?
		Java provides:
			Comparator.nullsFirst()
			Comparator.nullsLast()
		
	Γ£à Option 1: Put Nulls First
		List<Employee> sorted = employees.stream()
		    .sorted(Comparator.comparing(Employee::getAge)
		        .thenComparing(
		            Employee::getDepartment,
		            Comparator.nullsFirst(String::compareTo)
		        )
		        .thenComparing(Employee::getSalary))
		    .collect(Collectors.toList());

	=> Now:
			If department is null ΓÁÈ comes first
			No exception

13. find the maximun occuring of char in given string
	String s = "manjunath";
    Map<Character, Integer> map = new HashMap<>();

    for (char ch : s.toCharArray()){
        map.put(ch, map.getOrDefault(ch,0) + 1);
    }

        System.out.println(map);


        char maxChar = ' ';
        int maxCount = 0;

        for(Map.Entry<Character, Integer> entry : map.entrySet()) {

            if(entry.getValue() > maxCount) {
                maxCount = entry.getValue();
                maxChar = entry.getKey();
            }
        }

        System.out.println("Max occurring char: " + maxChar);
        System.out.println("Count: " + maxCount);

15. add array element one after other in new array

		int arr1[] = {1,2,3,4,5};
        int arr2[] = {6,7,8};

        int arr3[] = new int[arr1.length + arr2.length];

        int i = 0, j=0, k=0;

        while (i < arr1.length && j < arr2.length){
            arr3[k++] = arr1[i++];
            arr3[k++] = arr2[j++];
        }

        // Copy remaining elements (if any)
        while(i < arr1.length){
            arr3[k++] = arr1[i++];
        }

        while (j < arr2.length){
            arr3[k++] = arr2[j++];
        }

        Arrays.stream(arr3).forEach(n-> System.out.println(n)); //[1, 6, 2, 7, 3, 8, 4, 9, 5]
		
		(or)
		
		int arr1[] = {1,2,3,4,5};
        int arr2[] = {6,7,8};

        List<Integer>  list = new ArrayList<>(arr1.length + arr2.length);
        int i=0, j=0;
        while (i < arr1.length && j < arr2.length){
            list.add(arr1[i++]);
            list.add(arr2[j++]);
        }
        list.forEach(n-> System.out.println(n));

30. Reverse a string but keep spaces in the same positions.
	i/p : "I Am Not String"
	o/p : "g ni rtS toNm AI"

	    String input = "I Am Not String";

        char[] chars = input.toCharArray();

        int left = 0;
        int right = chars.length-1;

        while(left < right){
            if(chars[left] == ' '){
                left ++;
            } else if (chars[right] == ' ') {
                right ++;
            }else{
                char temp = chars[left];
                chars[left] = chars[right];
                chars[right] = temp;
                left ++;
                right --;
            }
        }
        System.out.println(chars);

32. Convert a binary number (e.g., 1011) to decimal.
	=>  = 1├ù2┬│ + 0├ù2┬▓ + 1├ù2┬╣ + 1├ù2Γü░
		= 8 + 0 + 2 + 1
		= 11

		 String binary = "1011";
	        int decimal = 0;
	        int power = 0;
	
	        for (int i = binary.length() - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
	            int bit = Integer.parseInt(String.valueOf(binary.charAt(i)));
	            decimal += bit * Math.pow(2, power);
	            power++;
	        }
	
	        System.out.println(decimal);


33.	What Is Binary Search ? 
	=> Binary Search is an algorithm used to: Efficiently search an element in a sorted array.

	2∩╕ÂΓâú Prerequisite (Very Important)
		≡ÓÀÊ Array/List must be sorted
				Ascending or descending ΓÇõ but sorted.
		If not sorted ΓÙÔ
			Binary search will give wrong result.

=> 	Principle of Binary Search
			Main idea:
				Divide the search space into half every time.
			Steps:
				Find middle element
				Compare target with middle
				If equal ΓÁÈ return
				If target < middle ΓÁÈ search left half
				If target > middle ΓÁÈ search right half
				Repeat
			This is called:
				≡ÓÀÊ Divide and Conquer

	=>  int[] arr = {10, 20, 30, 40, 50, 60};
        int target = 50;
        System.out.println(binarySearch(arr, target));+

	=>  public static int binarySearch(int[] arr, int target) {
	        int left = 0;
	        int right = arr.length - 1;
	
	        while (left <= right) {
	
	            int mid = (left + right)/2;
	
	            if (arr[mid] == target) {
	                return mid;
	            }
	
	            if (arr[mid] < target) {
	                left = mid + 1;
	            } else {
	                right = mid - 1;
	            }
	        }
	
	        return -1; // not found
	    }

	=> Time complexity : O(log n)
	   Space complexity : O(1)


34. How to print odd and even number using thread class ?

	public class Main {
	    public static void main(String[] args) {
	
	        printEvenOrOddNum printNum = new printEvenOrOddNum();
	
	        Thread oddThread = new Thread( () -> printNum.printOdd());
	        Thread eventThread = new Thread( ()-> printNum.printEven());
	    
	        oddThread.start();
	        eventThread.start();
	
	    }
	}

create another class
		public class printEvenOrOddNum {
	
	    private int number = 1;
	    private int limit = 10;
	
	    public synchronized void printOdd(){
	
	       while(number <= limit){
	
	           if(number%2 == 0){
	               try {
	                wait();
	               }catch (Exception e){
	                   e.printStackTrace();
	               }
	           }else{
	               System.out.println("odd" + number);
	               number ++;
	               notify();
	           }
	       }
	
	    }
	
	    public synchronized  void printEven(){
	
	        while (number <= limit ){
	            if(number%2 != 0){
	                try {
	                    wait();
	                }catch (Exception e){
	                    e.printStackTrace();
	                }
	            }else{
	                System.out.println("even" + number);
	                number++;
	                notify();
	            }
	        }
	
	    }
	}
	

35. How to multiply two number using funtional interface ?

	=> @FunctionalInterface
		public interface Multiple {
		    int multiple(int a, int b);
		}

	=> public class Main {
		    public static void main(String[] args) {
		        Multiple multi = (a,b) -> a * b;
		        int multiple = multi.multiple(10, 20);
		        System.out.println(multiple);  // 200
		    }
		}

36. Write a function to validate an Indian mobile number.

	 System.out.println(isValidateNumber("+917019684195")); 

	private static boolean isValidateNumber(String number) {
        if(number == null){
            return false;
        }

        if(number.startsWith("+91")){
            number = number.substring(3);
        } else if (number.startsWith("91")) {
            number = number.substring(2);
        }

        if (number.length() != 10){
            return false;
        }

        char firstDigit = number.charAt(0);

        if(firstDigit < '6' || firstDigit > '9' ){
            return false;
        }

        for (char c : number.toCharArray()){
            if(!Character.isDigit(c)){
                return false;
            }
        }
        return true;
    }

37.Find an index i such that the sum of elements on the left of equals the sum of elements on the right of i. (Equilibrium 	Index):
			 int[] arr = {1, 7, 3, 6, 5, 6};
		        int totalSum = 0;
		        int leftSum = 0;
		        
		        for (int val : arr){
		            totalSum += val;
		        }
		
		        for (int i = 0; i < arr.length; i++) {
		
		            int rightSum = totalSum - (leftSum + arr[i]);
		
		            if(leftSum == rightSum){
		                System.out.println("index ::" + i);
		                return;
		            }
		            leftSum += arr[i];
		
		        }
		        System.out.println("No equilibrium index found");

	Time Complexity :
	=> total Time
			O(n) + O(n)  -> since two loops
				Drop constants in Big-O:
			O(n)
		=> Γ£à Final Time Complexity = O(n)

	Space Complexity :
		=> Extra variables used:
				totalSum
				leftSum
				rightSum
				i
				
			=>	These are constant variables.
			=>  So memory used does NOT grow with input size.
			=>	Γ£à Space Complexity = O(1) (Constant Space)


38. two sum problem :

	    int[] arr = {2,11,7,15};
        int target = 9;

        for (int i = 0; i < arr.length; i++) {

            for (int j = i+1; j < arr.length; j++) {

                if(arr[i] + arr[j] == target){
                    System.out.println(i + " " +j);
                }
            }
        }

	=> Time Complexity : O(n┬▓)
	=> Space Complexity : O(1)

39. Find the missing number :
	int[] nums = {3,0,1};
	public static int findMissing(int[] nums) {
        int n = nums.length;
        int expectedSum = n * (n + 1) / 2;
        int actualSum = 0;
        for(int num : nums){
            actualSum += num;
        }
        return expectedSum - actualSum;
    }

	=> Time Complexity  : O(n)
	=> Space Complexity : O(1)

40. Maximum Subarray Sum :
		int[] nums = {-2,1,-3,4,-1,2,1,-5,4};
        int maxSum = 0;

        for (int i = 0; i < nums.length; i++) {
            int sum = 0;
            for (int j = i; j < nums.length; j++) {
                sum += nums[j];
                maxSum = Math.max(maxSum, sum);
            }
        }
        System.out.println(maxSum); //6

	=>	Time Complexity  : O(n┬▓)
	=> Space Complexity : O(1)

41. Given an array, rotate the array to the right by k steps.
	Input:
		nums = [1,2,3,4,5,6,7]           Output: [5,6,7,1,2,3,4]
		k = 3 

	 	int[] nums = {1,2,3,4,5,6,7};
        int k = 3;

        int[] result = new int[nums.length];
        for (int i = 0; i < nums.length; i++) {
            result[ (i+k)%nums.length] = nums[i];
        }

        for (int val : result){
            System.out.println(val);
        }  // [5,6,7,1,2,3,4]

	=> Time  : O(n)
	=> Space : O(n)

42. Merge two Array :
		int[] nums1 = {1,3,5};
        int[] nums2 = {2,4,6};

        int[] result = IntStream.concat(
                Arrays.stream(nums1),
                Arrays.stream(nums2)
        ).toArray();

        for (int val : result){
            System.out.print(val +" ");
        }

43. Stock Buy Sell :

		int[] prices = {7,1,5,3,6,4};
        int maxprofit = 0;

        for (int i = 0; i < prices.length; i++) {
            for (int j = i+1; j < prices.length; j++) {
                int profit = prices[j] - prices[i];
                maxprofit = Math.max(maxprofit, profit);
            }
        }

        System.out.println(maxprofit);

		=> prices[i] = price of a stock on day i
				You must:
					Γ£à Buy one day
					Γ£à Sell on a later day
					Γ£à Maximize profit
				Return the maximum profit.

		=> Time Complexity  : O(n┬▓)
		=> Space Complexity : O(1)

44. Longest Substring Without Repeating :
	 String s = "abcabcbb";
        int start = 0;
        int end = 0;
        int max_length = 0;

        List<Character> list = new ArrayList<>();
        while(end < s.length()){
            if(!list.contains(s.charAt(end))){
                list.add(s.charAt(end));
                max_length = Math.max(max_length, list.size());
                end++;
            }else{
                list.remove((Character)s.charAt(start));
                start++;
            }
        }
        System.out.println(max_length);

45. If an element appears more than once in the array, replace all occurrences of that element with #.
		 int[] arr = {6,7,8,5,3,5,6};
	        Map<Integer, Integer> map = new HashMap<>();
	        List<Object> list = new ArrayList<>();
	        
	        for (Integer val : arr){
	           map.put(val, map.getOrDefault(val,0)+ 1);
	        }
	        
	        for (Integer val : arr){
	            if(map.get(val)> 1){
	                list.add("#");
	            }else{
	                list.add(val);
	            }
	        }
	        
	        for (Object val : list){
	            System.out.println(val);  [#,7,8,#,3,#,#]
	        }

		
===================================================== Introduction ======================================================================
	
Hi, IΓÇÕm Roy. I have around 5.5 years of experience as a Full Stack Developer working mainly with Angular and Spring Boot.

==========================================================================================================================================
My project Architeture :

≡ÓõÀ Core Microservices in Your Project

1. ∩╕ÂClaim Service
		Entry point when a new insurance claim is submitted
		Performs basic validations
		Publishes claim event to Kafka
	
2. Fraud Service (Your Core Area)
		Consumes claim events
		Validates claim against internal fraud rules
		Calls external third-party systems (GAF) if data is missing
		Calculates and stores fraud scores
		
3. Litigation Service
		Handles legal cases, disputes, court-related info
		Triggered when fraud score crosses a threshold
		
4. External Integration Service
		Uses Feign Client
		Communicates with GAF / third-party fraud scoring systems
		Handles retries, timeouts, fallback
		
5. Kafka (Event Backbone)
		Enables loose coupling
		Handles high-volume claim processing
		Enables async communication
		
		
=> Our application follows a microservices and event-driven architecture in the insurance fraud and litigation domain.
	Whenever a claim is created, the Claim Service publishes a Kafka event. The Fraud Service consumes this event and validates 
	the claim against internal rules and historical data. If sufficient data is not available or itΓÇÕs a new claim type, 
	we synchronously call third-party fraud scoring systems like GAF using Feign Client.
	
	The external response provides fraud scores and risk indicators, which we persist in our database and use to make automated decisions.
	Based on configurable thresholds, claims either proceed normally or are escalated to the Litigation Service for manual investigation.
	
	Kafka ensures loose coupling, scalability, and resilience, while Feign handles external integrations with retries and circuit breakers
	
	
=> High-Level Microservices Architecture :

	                +-------------------+
                    |       UI /        |
                    |   API Gateway     |
                    +---------+---------+
                              |
                              v
                    +-------------------+
                    |    Claim Service  |
                    +---------+---------+
                              |
                              |  (Publish Event)
                              v
                    =========================
                    |        KAFKA          |
                    =========================
                              |
               +--------------+--------------+
               |                             |
               v                             v
     +-------------------+          +-------------------+
     |   Fraud Service   |          | Notification Svc  |
     +---------+---------+          +-------------------+
               |
               | (If data missing)
               v
        +--------------+
        |  GAF System  |  <-- External (Feign Client)
        +--------------+
               |
               v
        +--------------+
        |   Database   |
        +--------------+
               |
               v
        +-------------------+
        | Litigation Svc    |
        +-------------------+


1. how do we handle failures in Kafka while communicating between the services ?
	≡Óõ╣ 1. Producer Side Failure Handling (Claim Service) :
			When publishing claim events:
				Γ£à Retries
					Configure:
						retries=3
						retry.backoff.ms=1000
							=> If Kafka is temporarily unavailable, retry automatically

				Γ£à ACKs Configuration
						Use:
						acks=all
							=> Ensures message is written to all replicas ΓÁÈ prevents data loss

				Γ£à Idempotent Producer
						Avoid duplicate messages:
							=> enable.idempotence=true

				Γ£à Fallback Handling
						If Kafka is completely down:
						Store event in DB (Outbox pattern)
						Retry later via scheduler

				≡ÓÀÊ Interview one-liner:
				"We use retries, idempotent producers, and outbox pattern to ensure no event is lost during publishing."

		≡Óõ╣ 2. Kafka Broker Level (Cluster Reliability)
				Γ£à Replication Factor (ΓÊÑ 3)
					Prevents broker failure impact
				Γ£à Leader Election
					If broker goes down ΓÁÈ another takes over
				≡ÓÀÊ One-liner:
				"Kafka replication ensures high availability and fault tolerance at broker level."

		≡Óõ╣ 3. Consumer Side Failure Handling (Fraud Service) 
				Γ£à a. Manual Offset Commit
					We commit offset only after successful processing
					Prevents message loss
					ack.acknowledge(); // only after success
				Γ£à b. Retry Mechanism
					Use Spring Kafka Retry / @RetryableTopic
					Retry transient failures (like DB or API failure)

				Γ£à c. Dead Letter Topic (DLT)
					If message fails after retries:
					Send to DLT
					Avoid blocking the system
					≡ÓÀÊ Example:
					claim-topic ΓÁÈ retry-topic ΓÁÈ DLT
				Γ£à d. Idempotent Consumer
					Avoid duplicate processing:
					Use unique claimId
					Maintain processed records

				Γ£à e. Error Handling (External Calls)
					In your case (Feign + GAF):
					Use:
						Retry (Resilience4j)
						Circuit Breaker
						Fallback response
					≡ÓÀÊ Example:
						@Retry(name="gaf-service")
						@CircuitBreaker(name="gaf-service", fallbackMethod="fallback")

			=> We handle Kafka failures at multiple levels.
			   On the producer side, we use retries, idempotent producers, and the outbox pattern to avoid data loss.
			   Kafka cluster ensures reliability using replication.
			   On the consumer side, we use manual offset commits, retry mechanisms, and Dead Letter Topics for failed messages.
			   We also implement idempotency to avoid duplicate processing and use circuit breakers for external API failures.ΓÇÙ

	=> Retry mechanism in producer level :
				You configure this in application.yml / properties
					spring:
					  kafka:
					    producer:
					      retries: 3
					      properties:
					        retry.backoff.ms: 1000
							 enable.idempotence: true -> Prevents duplicate messages during retries
					      acks: all
					≡Óõì What this does:
					
					=> retries=3 ΓÁÈ retry sending message if broker fails
					=> retry.backoff.ms=1000 ΓÁÈ wait 1 sec between retries
					=> acks=all ΓÁÈ ensures message is written safely

			=> If Broker is down form long time, we cna store claim + event in DB and later we can push via scheduler
			Eg @Scheduled(fixedDelay = 5000)
				public void publishOutboxEvents() {
				    List<Event> events = repository.findPending();
				
				    for (Event e : events) {
				        kafkaTemplate.send("claim-topic", e);
				        e.setStatus("SENT");
				    }
				}

	=> Retry in comsumer level :
		Γ£à Using @RetryableTopic
		@RetryableTopic(
		    attempts = "4",
		    backoff = @Backoff(
		        delay = 5000,
		        multiplier = 2
		    ),
		    dltTopicSuffix = ".DLT"
		)
		@KafkaListener(topics = "claim-topic", groupId = "fraud-group")
		public void consume(ClaimEvent event) {
		    processClaim(event);
		}

=>  After max retries, the message is sent to a Dead Letter Topic.
	Once the external system is back, we reprocess DLT messages

	4. Exception Handling (VERY IMPORTANT ≡ÓõÑ) in call GAF's
			Retry + Circuit Breaker :
				@Retry(name = "gaf-service")
				@CircuitBreaker(name = "gaf-service", fallbackMethod = "fallback")
				public GafResponse callGaf(GafRequest request) {
				    return gafClient.getScore(request);
				}
				≡Óõ╣ Fallback Method
				public GafResponse fallback(GafRequest request, Exception ex) {
				    // default safe response
				    return new GafResponse(0, "UNKNOWN", List.of(), "REVIEW");
				}

6. Optimization Techniques We Follow ?
	1. Memory Optimization :
		Γ£à A. Lightweight DTOs (Kafka Events)
				≡ÓÀÊ We send only required fields, not full objects
			Γ£õ Reduces:
				Network payload
				Heap usage

		Γ£à B. Avoid Large Object Loading
				≡ÓÀÊ Example:
					DonΓÇÕt load full customer history
					Fetch only required fields
					@Query("SELECT c.claimId, c.amount FROM Claim c WHERE c.id = :id")

		Γ£à C. Streaming / Pagination
				≡ÓÀÊ For large data:
					Page<Claim> claims = repository.findAll(PageRequest.of(0, 50));
					Γ£õ Prevents OutOfMemoryError

		Γ£à D. Use Caching (Redis / In-Memory)
				≡ÓÀÊ Cache:
					Config (threshold)
					Frequently used data

	2. Thread Safety & Concurrency :
		Γ£à B. Kafka Consumer Concurrency
				spring:
				  kafka:
				    listener:
				      concurrency: 3
				≡ÓÀÊ Multiple threads consume messages
				Γ£õ Improves throughput

		Γ£à D. Database-Level Safety
				≡ÓÀÊ Use:
				Unique constraints
				Transactions
			@Transactional

		Γ£à F. Use Thread Pools (ExecutorService)
				≡ÓÀÊ Example:
					Sending emails
					Parallel processing
					ExecutorService executor = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(10);

		Γ£à Circuit Breaker
				Γ£õ Avoid wasting threads on failing service

		Γ£à ConcurantHashMap, syncronize keyword, Atomic variable, Completable future


	3. Database Optimization :
		Γ£à Indexing
			CREATE INDEX idx_claim_id ON claim(claim_id);
			Γ£õ Faster lookup
		Γ£à Connection Pooling (HikariCP)
			Γ£õ Reuse DB connections

7. How Do Services Trust Each Other ?
	-> we should forward the same JWT
	-> ≡Óõ╣ Why?
			Because:
				Downstream services (Fraud, Litigation) must:
				Know who the user is
				Know roles/permissions
				Perform authorization
	-> API Gateway
			Validates:
				Signature Γ£à
				Expiry Γ£à
				Issuer Γ£à
				≡ÓÀÊ If valid:
					Γ₧í∩╕Â Forward SAME JWT to Claim Service
	-> Claim Service
			Again validates JWT (zero-trust ≡ÓõÑ)
			Processes request

8. Are We Doing Tuning ?
		≡ÓÀÊ Yes ΓÇõ we do tuning at 3 levels:
			1. Thread Pool Tuning
			2. Connection Pooling
			3. JVM Tuning

	≡Óõ╣ 1. Thread Pool Tuning ≡Óº╡
			1. Kafka Consumer Threads
				spring:
				  kafka:
				    listener:
				      concurrency: 3
				≡ÓÀÊ Meaning:
					3 threads consume messages in parallel

			2. Async Tasks (Email / Notifications)
					Executor executor = new ThreadPoolTaskExecutor(10);

	≡Óõ╣ 2. Connection Pooling (DB) ≡Óùã∩╕Â
				≡ÓÀÊ We use HikariCP (default in Spring Boot)
						Γ£à Configuration yaml file
							spring:
							  datasource:
							    hikari:
							      maximum-pool-size: 10
							      minimum-idle: 5
							      idle-timeout: 30000
							      max-lifetime: 1800000
							≡ÓÃ» Why?
								Avoid creating DB connection every time ΓÙÔ
								Reuse connections Γ£à
								Improve performance

	≡Óõ╣ 3. JVM Tuning ΓÌò (Important)
				Γ£à Heap Size
						-Xms512m
						-Xmx1024m
					≡ÓÀÊ Prevent frequent resizing
				Γ£à Garbage Collection
						-XX:+UseG1GC
					≡ÓÀÊ Better for:
						Low latency
						Microservices
				Γ£à Monitoring
					Using:
						Actuator /metrics

1. student table and asked to group by name and calculate total marks, and display the result in descending order based on total marks.

		SELECT name, SUM(marks) AS total_marks
		FROM student
		GROUP BY name
		ORDER BY total_marks DESC;

2. Given a table containing task_id, start_time, and end_time, Write a query to fetch the events that occur more than once on the same day, and display the 		results in ascending order.

		SELECT 
	    task_id,
	    DATE(start_time) AS event_date,
	    COUNT(*) AS occurrence_count
		FROM tasks
		GROUP BY task_id, DATE(start_time)
		HAVING COUNT(*) > 1
		ORDER BY event_date ASC, task_id ASC;



22. binary search code ? what are the prerequeste ? what is the principles ? whar the other way can search

1. Explain your current project architecture

Question

Explain the architecture of your insurance project.

Answer

In our insurance application:

Angular UI
   ΓÁô
Spring Boot REST APIs
   ΓÁô
Service Layer (business logic)
   ΓÁô
JPA / Hibernate
   ΓÁô
Database (Oracle/PostgreSQL)

Angular handles UI and state management, while Spring Boot exposes REST APIs for claim processing, fraud investigation, and policy management. Hibernate manages database interactions.

2. How does Angular communicate with backend APIs?

Answer

Angular uses HttpClient service.

Example:

this.http.get('/api/claims');

In our insurance system, Angular calls APIs like:

GET /claims
POST /fraud-investigation
PUT /claim-status

The backend processes the request and returns JSON.

3. What is Dependency Injection in Angular?

Answer

Dependency Injection allows Angular to provide required services automatically.

Example in our project:

constructor(private claimService: ClaimService) {}

Angular injects ClaimService so the component can fetch insurance claim data.

4. What problem does NgRx solve?

Answer

NgRx provides centralized state management.

In our project:

Multiple components need claim data:

Claim List
Claim Details
Fraud Summary

Instead of calling APIs multiple times, NgRx stores the claim data in a global store.

5. Difference between switchMap and mergeMap in RxJS

Answer

switchMap cancels previous requests.

Example in insurance search:

User searches claims:

User types claimId quickly

switchMap cancels old requests and keeps only the latest search.

6. How does Spring Boot start internally?

Answer

Spring Boot startup flow:

SpringApplication.run()
   ΓÁô
ApplicationContext created
   ΓÁô
AutoConfiguration applied
   ΓÁô
Beans created
   ΓÁô
Embedded server started (Tomcat)
7. What is the difference between @Component, @Service, @Repository?

Answer

Annotation	Purpose
@Component	Generic component
@Service	Business logic
@Repository	Database access

Example in insurance system:

ClaimController
ClaimService
ClaimRepository
8. What happens inside HashMap when collision occurs?

Answer

HashMap uses:

hashCode()
ΓÁô
bucket index
ΓÁô
linked list / tree

If two claim IDs generate the same hash, they are stored in the same bucket.

Java 8 converts linked list ΓÁÈ Red Black Tree when collisions exceed 8.

9. What is ConcurrentHashMap?

Answer

ConcurrentHashMap supports thread-safe operations without locking the entire map.

Example:

In fraud detection service, multiple threads process claims simultaneously.

ConcurrentHashMap stores claim results safely.

10. What is an immutable class?

Answer

An immutable object cannot change after creation.

Example:

Insurance policy configuration object.

Example code:

final class PolicyConfig {
   private final String policyType;
}
11. How do you prevent race conditions?

Answer

Using:

synchronized
ReentrantLock
Atomic variables

Example:

Multiple threads updating claim status must synchronize updates.

12. Explain transaction isolation levels

Answer

Isolation levels prevent data inconsistency.

Example:

If two agents update the same claim simultaneously.

Isolation levels:

READ_COMMITTED
REPEATABLE_READ
SERIALIZABLE
13. What is the N+1 query problem?

Answer

N+1 occurs when JPA executes multiple queries unnecessarily.

Example:

Fetching claims and their policies:

1 query ΓÁÈ claims
N queries ΓÁÈ policies

Solution:

JOIN FETCH

18. What is optimistic locking?

Answer

Prevents conflicts using version numbers.

Example:

Two users editing the same claim.

If version mismatch occurs ΓÁÈ update fails.

19. What is pessimistic locking?

Answer

Locks the record during update.

Example:

Critical claim settlement updates.

11. What is the difference between wait() and sleep()?
wait()	sleep()
Releases lock	Does not release lock
Used in synchronization	Used for delay

Example:

Producer-consumer pattern in claim processing.

12. What causes memory leaks in Java?

Common reasons:

Static collections
Unclosed resources
Listeners not removed
Improper caching

Example:

Fraud detection service caching claim objects without eviction.

Solution:

WeakHashMap
Cache eviction
13. What is the difference between checked and unchecked exceptions?
Checked	Unchecked
Compile-time	Runtime
IOException	NullPointerException

Example:

Database connection failure ΓÁÈ checked exception
Null pointer bug ΓÁÈ unchecked
14. What is double-checked locking?

Used in Singleton pattern.

Example:

private static volatile Instance instance;

public static Instance getInstance(){
    if(instance == null){
        synchronized(ClassName.class){
            if(instance == null){
                instance = new Instance();
            }
        }
    }
    return instance;
}

Used when initializing:

Fraud detection engine
Configuration loader
15. Explain Producer Consumer problem

Classic multithreading problem.

Example in insurance system:

Claim requests incoming
ΓÁô
Queue
ΓÁô
Worker threads process claims

Example using blocking queue:

BlockingQueue<Claim> queue = new LinkedBlockingQueue<>();

Producer:

Adds claim request

Consumer:

Processes claim
